3372 
3373         /**
3374          * Find my trustable caller class if m is a caller sensitive method.
3375          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3376          * Otherwise, if m is caller-sensitive, throw IllegalAccessException.
3377          */
3378         Lookup findBoundCallerLookup(MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3379             if (MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(m) && !hasFullPrivilegeAccess()) {
3380                 // Only lookups with full privilege access are allowed to resolve caller-sensitive methods
3381                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3382             }
3383             return this;
3384         }
3385 
3386         /**
3387          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3388          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3389          *
3390          * @deprecated This method was originally designed to test {@code PRIVATE} access
3391          * that implies full privilege access but {@code MODULE} access has since become
3392          * independent of {@code PRIVATE} access.  It is recommended to call
3393          * {@link #hasFullPrivilegeAccess()} instead.
3394          * @since 9
3395          */
3396         @Deprecated(since="14")
3397         public boolean hasPrivateAccess() {
3398             return hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3399         }
3400 
3401         /**
3402          * Returns {@code true} if this lookup has <em>full privilege access</em>,
3403          * i.e. {@code PRIVATE} and {@code MODULE} access.
3404          * A {@code Lookup} object must have full privilege access in order to
3405          * access all members that are allowed to the {@linkplain #lookupClass() lookup class}.
3406          *
3407          * @return {@code true} if this lookup has full privilege access.
3408          * @since 14
3409          * @see <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#privacc">private and module access</a>
3410          */
3411         public boolean hasFullPrivilegeAccess() {
3412             return (allowedModes & (PRIVATE|MODULE)) == (PRIVATE|MODULE);
3413         }
3414 
3415         /**
3416          * Perform necessary <a href="MethodHandles.Lookup.html#secmgr">access checks</a>.
3417          * Determines a trustable caller class to compare with refc, the symbolic reference class.
3418          * If this lookup object has full privilege access, then the caller class is the lookupClass.
3419          */
3420         void checkSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3421             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3422 
3423             SecurityManager smgr = System.getSecurityManager();
3424             if (smgr == null)  return;
3425 
3426             // Step 1:
3427             boolean fullPowerLookup = hasFullPrivilegeAccess();
3428             if (!fullPowerLookup ||
3429                 !VerifyAccess.classLoaderIsAncestor(lookupClass, refc)) {
3430                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(refc);
3431             }
3432 
3433             if (m == null) {  // findClass or accessClass
3434                 // Step 2b:
3435                 if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3436                     smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.GET_CLASSLOADER_PERMISSION);
3437                 }
3438                 return;
3439             }
3440 
3441             // Step 2a:
3442             if (m.isPublic()) return;
3443             if (!fullPowerLookup) {
3444                 smgr.checkPermission(SecurityConstants.CHECK_MEMBER_ACCESS_PERMISSION);
3445             }
3446 
3447             // Step 3:
3448             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3449             if (!fullPowerLookup && defc != refc) {
3450                 ReflectUtil.checkPackageAccess(defc);
3451             }
3452         }
3453 
3454         void checkMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3455             boolean wantStatic = (refKind == REF_invokeStatic);
3456             String message;
3457             if (m.isConstructor())
3458                 message = "expected a method, not a constructor";
3459             else if (!m.isMethod())
3460                 message = "expected a method";
3461             else if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3462                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static method" : "expected a non-static method";
3463             else
3464                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3465             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3466         }
3467 
3468         void checkField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3469             boolean wantStatic = !MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind);
3470             String message;
3471             if (wantStatic != m.isStatic())
3472                 message = wantStatic ? "expected a static field" : "expected a non-static field";
3473             else
3474                 { checkAccess(refKind, refc, m); return; }
3475             throw m.makeAccessException(message, this);
3476         }
3477 
3478         /** Check public/protected/private bits on the symbolic reference class and its member. */
3479         void checkAccess(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName m) throws IllegalAccessException {
3480             assert(m.referenceKindIsConsistentWith(refKind) &&
3481                    MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsValid(refKind) &&
3482                    (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind) == m.isField()));
3483             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3484             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3485             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3486             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) &&
3487                     refKind == REF_invokeVirtual &&
3488                     m.getDeclaringClass() == Object.class &&
3489                     m.getName().equals("clone") &&
3490                     refc.isArray()) {
3491                 // The JVM does this hack also.
3492                 // (See ClassVerifier::verify_invoke_instructions
3493                 // and LinkResolver::check_method_accessability.)
3494                 // Because the JVM does not allow separate methods on array types,
3495                 // there is no separate method for int[].clone.
3496                 // All arrays simply inherit Object.clone.
3497                 // But for access checking logic, we make Object.clone
3498                 // (normally protected) appear to be public.
3499                 // Later on, when the DirectMethodHandle is created,
3500                 // its leading argument will be restricted to the
3501                 // requested array type.
3502                 // N.B. The return type is not adjusted, because
3503                 // that is *not* the bytecode behavior.
3504                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED | Modifier.PUBLIC;
3505             }
3506             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods) && refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3507                 // cannot "new" a protected ctor in a different package
3508                 mods ^= Modifier.PROTECTED;
3509             }
3510             if (Modifier.isFinal(mods) &&
3511                     MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(refKind))
3512                 throw m.makeAccessException("unexpected set of a final field", this);
3513             int requestedModes = fixmods(mods);  // adjust 0 => PACKAGE
3514             if ((requestedModes & allowedModes) != 0) {
3515                 if (VerifyAccess.isMemberAccessible(refc, m.getDeclaringClass(),
3516                                                     mods, lookupClass(), previousLookupClass(), allowedModes))
3517                     return;
3518             } else {
3519                 // Protected members can also be checked as if they were package-private.
3520                 if ((requestedModes & PROTECTED) != 0 && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0
3521                         && VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(m.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3522                     return;
3523             }
3524             throw m.makeAccessException(accessFailedMessage(refc, m), this);
3525         }
3526 
3527         String accessFailedMessage(Class<?> refc, MemberName m) {
3528             Class<?> defc = m.getDeclaringClass();
3529             int mods = m.getModifiers();
3530             // check the class first:
3531             boolean classOK = (Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) &&
3532                                (defc == refc ||
3533                                 Modifier.isPublic(refc.getModifiers())));
3534             if (!classOK && (allowedModes & PACKAGE) != 0) {
3535                 // ignore previous lookup class to check if default package access
3536                 classOK = (VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(defc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES) &&
3537                            (defc == refc ||
3538                             VerifyAccess.isClassAccessible(refc, lookupClass(), null, FULL_POWER_MODES)));
3539             }
3540             if (!classOK)
3541                 return "class is not public";
3542             if (Modifier.isPublic(mods))
3543                 return "access to public member failed";  // (how?, module not readable?)
3544             if (Modifier.isPrivate(mods))
3545                 return "member is private";
3546             if (Modifier.isProtected(mods))
3547                 return "member is protected";
3548             return "member is private to package";
3549         }
3550 
3551         private void checkSpecialCaller(Class<?> specialCaller, Class<?> refc) throws IllegalAccessException {
3552             int allowedModes = this.allowedModes;
3553             if (allowedModes == TRUSTED)  return;
3554             if ((lookupModes() & PRIVATE) == 0
3555                 || (specialCaller != lookupClass()
3556                        // ensure non-abstract methods in superinterfaces can be special-invoked
3557                     && !(refc != null && refc.isInterface() && refc.isAssignableFrom(specialCaller))))
3558                 throw new MemberName(specialCaller).
3559                     makeAccessException("no private access for invokespecial", this);
3560         }
3561 
3562         private boolean restrictProtectedReceiver(MemberName method) {
3563             // The accessing class only has the right to use a protected member
3564             // on itself or a subclass.  Enforce that restriction, from JVMS 5.4.4, etc.
3565             if (!method.isProtected() || method.isStatic()
3566                 || allowedModes == TRUSTED
3567                 || method.getDeclaringClass() == lookupClass()
3568                 || VerifyAccess.isSamePackage(method.getDeclaringClass(), lookupClass()))
3569                 return false;
3570             return true;
3571         }
3572         private MethodHandle restrictReceiver(MemberName method, DirectMethodHandle mh, Class<?> caller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3573             assert(!method.isStatic());
3574             // receiver type of mh is too wide; narrow to caller
3575             if (!method.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(caller)) {
3576                 throw method.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", caller);
3577             }
3578             MethodType rawType = mh.type();
3579             if (caller.isAssignableFrom(rawType.parameterType(0))) return mh; // no need to restrict; already narrow
3580             MethodType narrowType = rawType.changeParameterType(0, caller);
3581             assert(!mh.isVarargsCollector());  // viewAsType will lose varargs-ness
3582             assert(mh.viewAsTypeChecks(narrowType, true));
3583             return mh.copyWith(narrowType, mh.form);
3584         }
3585 
3586         /** Check access and get the requested method. */
3587         private MethodHandle getDirectMethod(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3588             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3589             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3590             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3591         }
3592         /** Check access and get the requested method, for invokespecial with no restriction on the application of narrowing rules. */
3593         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoRestrictInvokeSpecial(Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3594             final boolean doRestrict    = false;
3595             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3596             return getDirectMethodCommon(REF_invokeSpecial, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3597         }
3598         /** Check access and get the requested method, eliding security manager checks. */
3599         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method, Lookup callerLookup) throws IllegalAccessException {
3600             final boolean doRestrict    = true;
3601             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3602             return getDirectMethodCommon(refKind, refc, method, checkSecurity, doRestrict, callerLookup);
3603         }
3604         /** Common code for all methods; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3605         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName method,
3606                                                    boolean checkSecurity,
3607                                                    boolean doRestrict,
3608                                                    Lookup boundCaller) throws IllegalAccessException {
3609             checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3610             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3611             if (checkSecurity)
3612                 checkSecurityManager(refc, method);
3613             assert(!method.isMethodHandleInvoke());
3614 
3615             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial &&
3616                 refc != lookupClass() &&
3617                 !refc.isInterface() &&
3618                 refc != lookupClass().getSuperclass() &&
3619                 refc.isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3620                 assert(!method.getName().equals("<init>"));  // not this code path
3621 
3622                 // Per JVMS 6.5, desc. of invokespecial instruction:
3623                 // If the method is in a superclass of the LC,
3624                 // and if our original search was above LC.super,
3625                 // repeat the search (symbolic lookup) from LC.super
3626                 // and continue with the direct superclass of that class,
3627                 // and so forth, until a match is found or no further superclasses exist.
3628                 // FIXME: MemberName.resolve should handle this instead.
3629                 Class<?> refcAsSuper = lookupClass();
3630                 MemberName m2;
3631                 do {
3632                     refcAsSuper = refcAsSuper.getSuperclass();
3633                     m2 = new MemberName(refcAsSuper,
3634                                         method.getName(),
3635                                         method.getMethodType(),
3636                                         REF_invokeSpecial);
3637                     m2 = IMPL_NAMES.resolveOrNull(refKind, m2, lookupClassOrNull());
3638                 } while (m2 == null &&         // no method is found yet
3639                          refc != refcAsSuper); // search up to refc
3640                 if (m2 == null)  throw new InternalError(method.toString());
3641                 method = m2;
3642                 refc = refcAsSuper;
3643                 // redo basic checks
3644                 checkMethod(refKind, refc, method);
3645             }
3646             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refKind, refc, method, lookupClass());
3647             MethodHandle mh = dmh;
3648             // Optionally narrow the receiver argument to lookupClass using restrictReceiver.
3649             if ((doRestrict && refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) ||
3650                     (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) && restrictProtectedReceiver(method))) {
3651                 mh = restrictReceiver(method, dmh, lookupClass());
3652             }
3653             mh = maybeBindCaller(method, mh, boundCaller);
3654             mh = mh.setVarargs(method);
3655             return mh;
3656         }
3657         private MethodHandle maybeBindCaller(MemberName method, MethodHandle mh, Lookup boundCaller)
3658                                              throws IllegalAccessException {
3659             if (boundCaller.allowedModes == TRUSTED || !MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(method))
3660                 return mh;
3661 
3662             // boundCaller must have full privilege access.
3663             // It should have been checked by findBoundCallerLookup. Safe to check this again.
3664             if (!boundCaller.hasFullPrivilegeAccess())
3665                 throw new IllegalAccessException("Attempt to lookup caller-sensitive method using restricted lookup object");
3666 
3667             MethodHandle cbmh = MethodHandleImpl.bindCaller(mh, boundCaller.lookupClass);
3668             // Note: caller will apply varargs after this step happens.
3669             return cbmh;
3670         }
3671 
3672         /** Check access and get the requested field. */
3673         private MethodHandle getDirectField(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3674             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3675             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3676         }
3677         /** Check access and get the requested field, eliding security manager checks. */
3678         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field) throws IllegalAccessException {
3679             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3680             return getDirectFieldCommon(refKind, refc, field, checkSecurity);
3681         }
3682         /** Common code for all fields; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3683         private MethodHandle getDirectFieldCommon(byte refKind, Class<?> refc, MemberName field,
3684                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3685             checkField(refKind, refc, field);
3686             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3687             if (checkSecurity)
3688                 checkSecurityManager(refc, field);
3689             DirectMethodHandle dmh = DirectMethodHandle.make(refc, field);
3690             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(refKind) &&
3691                                     restrictProtectedReceiver(field));
3692             if (doRestrict)
3693                 return restrictReceiver(field, dmh, lookupClass());
3694             return dmh;
3695         }
3696         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandle(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3697                                             Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3698                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3699             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3700             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3701         }
3702         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleNoSecurityManager(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3703                                                              Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField)
3704                 throws IllegalAccessException {
3705             final boolean checkSecurity = false;
3706             return getFieldVarHandleCommon(getRefKind, putRefKind, refc, getField, putField, checkSecurity);
3707         }
3708         private VarHandle getFieldVarHandleCommon(byte getRefKind, byte putRefKind,
3709                                                   Class<?> refc, MemberName getField, MemberName putField,
3710                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3711             assert getField.isStatic() == putField.isStatic();
3712             assert getField.isGetter() && putField.isSetter();
3713             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(getRefKind) == MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsStatic(putRefKind);
3714             assert MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsGetter(getRefKind) && MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsSetter(putRefKind);
3715 
3716             checkField(getRefKind, refc, getField);
3717             if (checkSecurity)
3718                 checkSecurityManager(refc, getField);
3719 
3720             if (!putField.isFinal()) {
3721                 // A VarHandle does not support updates to final fields, any
3722                 // such VarHandle to a final field will be read-only and
3723                 // therefore the following write-based accessibility checks are
3724                 // only required for non-final fields
3725                 checkField(putRefKind, refc, putField);
3726                 if (checkSecurity)
3727                     checkSecurityManager(refc, putField);
3728             }
3729 
3730             boolean doRestrict = (MethodHandleNatives.refKindHasReceiver(getRefKind) &&
3731                                   restrictProtectedReceiver(getField));
3732             if (doRestrict) {
3733                 assert !getField.isStatic();
3734                 // receiver type of VarHandle is too wide; narrow to caller
3735                 if (!getField.getDeclaringClass().isAssignableFrom(lookupClass())) {
3736                     throw getField.makeAccessException("caller class must be a subclass below the method", lookupClass());
3737                 }
3738                 refc = lookupClass();
3739             }
3740             return VarHandles.makeFieldHandle(getField, refc, getField.getFieldType(),
3741                                              this.allowedModes == TRUSTED && !getField.getDeclaringClass().isHidden());
3742         }
3743         /** Check access and get the requested constructor. */
3744         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructor(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3745             final boolean checkSecurity = true;
3746             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3747         }
3748         /** Check access and get the requested constructor, eliding security manager checks. */
3749         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor) throws IllegalAccessException {
3750             final boolean checkSecurity = false;  // not needed for reflection or for linking CONSTANT_MH constants
3751             return getDirectConstructorCommon(refc, ctor, checkSecurity);
3752         }
3753         /** Common code for all constructors; do not call directly except from immediately above. */
3754         private MethodHandle getDirectConstructorCommon(Class<?> refc, MemberName ctor,
3755                                                   boolean checkSecurity) throws IllegalAccessException {
3756             assert(ctor.isConstructor());
3757             checkAccess(REF_newInvokeSpecial, refc, ctor);
3758             // Optionally check with the security manager; this isn't needed for unreflect* calls.
3759             if (checkSecurity)
3760                 checkSecurityManager(refc, ctor);
3761             assert(!MethodHandleNatives.isCallerSensitive(ctor));  // maybeBindCaller not relevant here
3762             return DirectMethodHandle.make(ctor).setVarargs(ctor);
3763         }
3764 
3765         /** Hook called from the JVM (via MethodHandleNatives) to link MH constants:
3766          */
3767         /*non-public*/
3768         MethodHandle linkMethodHandleConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, String name, Object type)
3769                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3770             if (!(type instanceof Class || type instanceof MethodType))
3771                 throw new InternalError("unresolved MemberName");
3772             MemberName member = new MemberName(refKind, defc, name, type);
3773             MethodHandle mh = LOOKASIDE_TABLE.get(member);
3774             if (mh != null) {
3775                 checkSymbolicClass(defc);
3776                 return mh;
3777             }
3778             if (defc == MethodHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3779                 // Treat MethodHandle.invoke and invokeExact specially.
3780                 mh = findVirtualForMH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3781                 if (mh != null) {
3782                     return mh;
3783                 }
3784             } else if (defc == VarHandle.class && refKind == REF_invokeVirtual) {
3785                 // Treat signature-polymorphic methods on VarHandle specially.
3786                 mh = findVirtualForVH(member.getName(), member.getMethodType());
3787                 if (mh != null) {
3788                     return mh;
3789                 }
3790             }
3791             MemberName resolved = resolveOrFail(refKind, member);
3792             mh = getDirectMethodForConstant(refKind, defc, resolved);
3793             if (mh instanceof DirectMethodHandle
3794                     && canBeCached(refKind, defc, resolved)) {
3795                 MemberName key = mh.internalMemberName();
3796                 if (key != null) {
3797                     key = key.asNormalOriginal();
3798                 }
3799                 if (member.equals(key)) {  // better safe than sorry
3800                     LOOKASIDE_TABLE.put(key, (DirectMethodHandle) mh);
3801                 }
3802             }
3803             return mh;
3804         }
3805         private boolean canBeCached(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member) {
3806             if (refKind == REF_invokeSpecial) {
3807                 return false;
3808             }
3809             if (!Modifier.isPublic(defc.getModifiers()) ||
3810                     !Modifier.isPublic(member.getDeclaringClass().getModifiers()) ||
3811                     !member.isPublic() ||
3812                     member.isCallerSensitive()) {
3813                 return false;
3814             }
3815             ClassLoader loader = defc.getClassLoader();
3816             if (loader != null) {
3817                 ClassLoader sysl = ClassLoader.getSystemClassLoader();
3818                 boolean found = false;
3819                 while (sysl != null) {
3820                     if (loader == sysl) { found = true; break; }
3821                     sysl = sysl.getParent();
3822                 }
3823                 if (!found) {
3824                     return false;
3825                 }
3826             }
3827             try {
3828                 MemberName resolved2 = publicLookup().resolveOrNull(refKind,
3829                     new MemberName(refKind, defc, member.getName(), member.getType()));
3830                 if (resolved2 == null) {
3831                     return false;
3832                 }
3833                 checkSecurityManager(defc, resolved2);
3834             } catch (SecurityException ex) {
3835                 return false;
3836             }
3837             return true;
3838         }
3839         private MethodHandle getDirectMethodForConstant(byte refKind, Class<?> defc, MemberName member)
3840                 throws ReflectiveOperationException {
3841             if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsField(refKind)) {
3842                 return getDirectFieldNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member);
3843             } else if (MethodHandleNatives.refKindIsMethod(refKind)) {
3844                 return getDirectMethodNoSecurityManager(refKind, defc, member, findBoundCallerLookup(member));
3845             } else if (refKind == REF_newInvokeSpecial) {
3846                 return getDirectConstructorNoSecurityManager(defc, member);
3847             }
3848             // oops
3849             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad MethodHandle constant #"+member);
3850         }
3851 
3852         static ConcurrentHashMap<MemberName, DirectMethodHandle> LOOKASIDE_TABLE = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();
3853     }
3854 
3855     /**
3856      * Produces a method handle constructing arrays of a desired type,
3857      * as if by the {@code anewarray} bytecode.
3858      * The return type of the method handle will be the array type.
3859      * The type of its sole argument will be {@code int}, which specifies the size of the array.
3860      *
3861      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a negative
3862      * array size, a {@code NegativeArraySizeException} will be thrown.
3863      *
3864      * @param arrayClass an array type
3865      * @return a method handle which can create arrays of the given type
3866      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3867      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code arrayClass} is not an array type
3868      * @see java.lang.reflect.Array#newInstance(Class, int)
3869      * @jvms 6.5 {@code anewarray} Instruction
3870      * @since 9
3871      */
3872     public static MethodHandle arrayConstructor(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3873         if (!arrayClass.isArray()) {
3874             throw newIllegalArgumentException("not an array class: " + arrayClass.getName());
3875         }
3876         MethodHandle ani = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_Array_newInstance).
3877                 bindTo(arrayClass.getComponentType());
3878         return ani.asType(ani.type().changeReturnType(arrayClass));
3879     }
3880 
3881     /**
3882      * Produces a method handle returning the length of an array,
3883      * as if by the {@code arraylength} bytecode.
3884      * The type of the method handle will have {@code int} as return type,
3885      * and its sole argument will be the array type.
3886      *
3887      * <p> If the returned method handle is invoked with a {@code null}
3888      * array reference, a {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown.
3889      *
3890      * @param arrayClass an array type
3891      * @return a method handle which can retrieve the length of an array of the given array type
3892      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is {@code null}
3893      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3894      * @jvms 6.5 {@code arraylength} Instruction
3895      * @since 9
3896      */
3897     public static MethodHandle arrayLength(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3898         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.LENGTH);
3899     }

3901     /**
3902      * Produces a method handle giving read access to elements of an array,
3903      * as if by the {@code aaload} bytecode.
3904      * The type of the method handle will have a return type of the array's
3905      * element type.  Its first argument will be the array type,
3906      * and the second will be {@code int}.
3907      *
3908      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3909      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3910      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3911      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3912      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3913      * the length of the array.
3914      *
3915      * @param arrayClass an array type
3916      * @return a method handle which can load values from the given array type
3917      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3918      * @throws  IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3919      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aaload} Instruction
3920      */
3921     public static MethodHandle arrayElementGetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3922         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.GET);
3923     }

3925     /**
3926      * Produces a method handle giving write access to elements of an array,
3927      * as if by the {@code astore} bytecode.
3928      * The type of the method handle will have a void return type.
3929      * Its last argument will be the array's element type.
3930      * The first and second arguments will be the array type and int.
3931      *
3932      * <p> When the returned method handle is invoked,
3933      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3934      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3935      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3936      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3937      * the length of the array.
3938      *
3939      * @param arrayClass the class of an array
3940      * @return a method handle which can store values into the array type
3941      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
3942      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
3943      * @jvms 6.5 {@code aastore} Instruction
3944      */
3945     public static MethodHandle arrayElementSetter(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
3946         return MethodHandleImpl.makeArrayElementAccessor(arrayClass, MethodHandleImpl.ArrayAccess.SET);
3947     }
3948 
3949     /**
3950      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array of type
3951      * {@code arrayClass}.  The VarHandle's variable type is the component type
3952      * of {@code arrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
3953      * {@code (arrayClass, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
3954      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into an array.
3955      * <p>
3956      * Certain access modes of the returned VarHandle are unsupported under
3957      * the following conditions:
3958      * <ul>
3959      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code byte},
3960      *     {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long},
3961      *     {@code float}, or {@code double} then numeric atomic update access
3962      *     modes are unsupported.
3963      * <li>if the component type is anything other than {@code boolean},
3964      *     {@code byte}, {@code short}, {@code char}, {@code int} or
3965      *     {@code long} then bitwise atomic update access modes are
3966      *     unsupported.
3967      * </ul>
3968      * <p>
3969      * If the component type is {@code float} or {@code double} then numeric
3970      * and atomic update access modes compare values using their bitwise
3971      * representation (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
3972      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
3973      *
3974      * <p> When the returned {@code VarHandle} is invoked,
3975      * the array reference and array index are checked.
3976      * A {@code NullPointerException} will be thrown if the array reference
3977      * is {@code null} and an {@code ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException} will be
3978      * thrown if the index is negative or if it is greater than or equal to
3979      * the length of the array.
3980      *
3981      * @apiNote
3982      * Bitwise comparison of {@code float} values or {@code double} values,
3983      * as performed by the numeric and atomic update access modes, differ
3984      * from the primitive {@code ==} operator and the {@link Float#equals}
3985      * and {@link Double#equals} methods, specifically with respect to
3986      * comparing NaN values or comparing {@code -0.0} with {@code +0.0}.
3987      * Care should be taken when performing a compare and set or a compare
3988      * and exchange operation with such values since the operation may
3989      * unexpectedly fail.
3990      * There are many possible NaN values that are considered to be
3991      * {@code NaN} in Java, although no IEEE 754 floating-point operation
3992      * provided by Java can distinguish between them.  Operation failure can
3993      * occur if the expected or witness value is a NaN value and it is
3994      * transformed (perhaps in a platform specific manner) into another NaN
3995      * value, and thus has a different bitwise representation (see
3996      * {@link Float#intBitsToFloat} or {@link Double#longBitsToDouble} for more
3997      * details).
3998      * The values {@code -0.0} and {@code +0.0} have different bitwise
3999      * representations but are considered equal when using the primitive
4000      * {@code ==} operator.  Operation failure can occur if, for example, a
4001      * numeric algorithm computes an expected value to be say {@code -0.0}
4002      * and previously computed the witness value to be say {@code +0.0}.
4003      * @param arrayClass the class of an array, of type {@code T[]}
4004      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of an array
4005      * @throws NullPointerException if the arrayClass is null
4006      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if arrayClass is not an array type
4007      * @since 9
4008      */
4009     public static VarHandle arrayElementVarHandle(Class<?> arrayClass) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4010         return VarHandles.makeArrayElementHandle(arrayClass);
4011     }
4012 
4013     /**
4014      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4015      * viewed as if it were a different primitive array type, such as
4016      * {@code int[]} or {@code long[]}.
4017      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4018      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4019      * {@code (byte[], int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4020      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4021      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a {@code byte[]}
4022      * array, composing bytes to or from a value of the component type of
4023      * {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4024      * <p>
4025      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4026      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4027      * {@code double}.
4028      * <p>
4029      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4030      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4031      * or greater than the {@code byte[]} array length minus the size (in bytes)
4032      * of {@code T}.
4033      * <p>
4034      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4035      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4036      * with the array and index.
4037      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4038      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4039      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4040      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4041      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4042      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4043      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4044      * <ul>
4045      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4046      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4047      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4048      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4049      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4050      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4051      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4052      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4053      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4054      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4055      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4056      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4057      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4058      * </ul>
4059      * <p>
4060      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4061      * for {@code byte[]} arrays without operating on a specific array.  Given
4062      * an {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4063      * {@code T_BOX}, misalignment may be determined as follows:
4064      * <pre>{@code
4065      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4066      * int misalignedAtZeroIndex = ByteBuffer.wrap(new byte[0]).
4067      *     alignmentOffset(0, sizeOfT);
4068      * int misalignedAtIndex = (misalignedAtZeroIndex + index) % sizeOfT;
4069      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4070      * }</pre>
4071      * <p>
4072      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4073      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4074      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4075      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4076      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4077      * type {@code T}
4078      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4079      * stored in the underlying {@code byte} array
4080      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code byte[]} array
4081      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4082      * array class
4083      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4084      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4085      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4086      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4087      * @since 9
4088      */
4089     public static VarHandle byteArrayViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4090                                      ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4091         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4092         return VarHandles.byteArrayViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4093                                               byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4094     }
4095 
4096     /**
4097      * Produces a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4098      * viewed as if it were an array of elements of a different primitive
4099      * component type to that of {@code byte}, such as {@code int[]} or
4100      * {@code long[]}.
4101      * The VarHandle's variable type is the component type of
4102      * {@code viewArrayClass} and the list of coordinate types is
4103      * {@code (ByteBuffer, int)}, where the {@code int} coordinate type
4104      * corresponds to an argument that is an index into a {@code byte[]} array.
4105      * The returned VarHandle accesses bytes at an index in a
4106      * {@code ByteBuffer}, composing bytes to or from a value of the component
4107      * type of {@code viewArrayClass} according to the given endianness.
4108      * <p>
4109      * The supported component types (variables types) are {@code short},
4110      * {@code char}, {@code int}, {@code long}, {@code float} and
4111      * {@code double}.
4112      * <p>
4113      * Access will result in a {@code ReadOnlyBufferException} for anything
4114      * other than the read access modes if the {@code ByteBuffer} is read-only.
4115      * <p>
4116      * Access of bytes at a given index will result in an
4117      * {@code IndexOutOfBoundsException} if the index is less than {@code 0}
4118      * or greater than the {@code ByteBuffer} limit minus the size (in bytes) of
4119      * {@code T}.
4120      * <p>
4121      * Access of bytes at an index may be aligned or misaligned for {@code T},
4122      * with respect to the underlying memory address, {@code A} say, associated
4123      * with the {@code ByteBuffer} and index.
4124      * If access is misaligned then access for anything other than the
4125      * {@code get} and {@code set} access modes will result in an
4126      * {@code IllegalStateException}.  In such cases atomic access is only
4127      * guaranteed with respect to the largest power of two that divides the GCD
4128      * of {@code A} and the size (in bytes) of {@code T}.
4129      * If access is aligned then following access modes are supported and are
4130      * guaranteed to support atomic access:
4131      * <ul>
4132      * <li>read write access modes for all {@code T}, with the exception of
4133      *     access modes {@code get} and {@code set} for {@code long} and
4134      *     {@code double} on 32-bit platforms.
4135      * <li>atomic update access modes for {@code int}, {@code long},
4136      *     {@code float} or {@code double}.
4137      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4138      *     types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4139      * <li>numeric atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4140      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4141      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4142      * <li>bitwise atomic update access modes for {@code int} and {@code long}.
4143      *     (Future major platform releases of the JDK may support additional
4144      *     numeric types for certain currently unsupported access modes.)
4145      * </ul>
4146      * <p>
4147      * Misaligned access, and therefore atomicity guarantees, may be determined
4148      * for a {@code ByteBuffer}, {@code bb} (direct or otherwise), an
4149      * {@code index}, {@code T} and it's corresponding boxed type,
4150      * {@code T_BOX}, as follows:
4151      * <pre>{@code
4152      * int sizeOfT = T_BOX.BYTES;  // size in bytes of T
4153      * ByteBuffer bb = ...
4154      * int misalignedAtIndex = bb.alignmentOffset(index, sizeOfT);
4155      * boolean isMisaligned = misalignedAtIndex != 0;
4156      * }</pre>
4157      * <p>
4158      * If the variable type is {@code float} or {@code double} then atomic
4159      * update access modes compare values using their bitwise representation
4160      * (see {@link Float#floatToRawIntBits} and
4161      * {@link Double#doubleToRawLongBits}, respectively).
4162      * @param viewArrayClass the view array class, with a component type of
4163      * type {@code T}
4164      * @param byteOrder the endianness of the view array elements, as
4165      * stored in the underlying {@code ByteBuffer} (Note this overrides the
4166      * endianness of a {@code ByteBuffer})
4167      * @return a VarHandle giving access to elements of a {@code ByteBuffer}
4168      * viewed as if elements corresponding to the components type of the view
4169      * array class
4170      * @throws NullPointerException if viewArrayClass or byteOrder is null
4171      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if viewArrayClass is not an array type
4172      * @throws UnsupportedOperationException if the component type of
4173      * viewArrayClass is not supported as a variable type
4174      * @since 9
4175      */
4176     public static VarHandle byteBufferViewVarHandle(Class<?> viewArrayClass,
4177                                       ByteOrder byteOrder) throws IllegalArgumentException {
4178         Objects.requireNonNull(byteOrder);
4179         return VarHandles.makeByteBufferViewHandle(viewArrayClass,
4180                                                    byteOrder == ByteOrder.BIG_ENDIAN);
4181     }
4182 
4183 
4184     /// method handle invocation (reflective style)
4185 
4186     /**
4187      * Produces a method handle which will invoke any method handle of the
4188      * given {@code type}, with a given number of trailing arguments replaced by
4189      * a single trailing {@code Object[]} array.
4190      * The resulting invoker will be a method handle with the following
4191      * arguments:
4192      * <ul>
4193      * <li>a single {@code MethodHandle} target
4194      * <li>zero or more leading values (counted by {@code leadingArgCount})
4195      * <li>an {@code Object[]} array containing trailing arguments
4196      * </ul>
4197      * <p>
4198      * The invoker will invoke its target like a call to {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke} with
4199      * the indicated {@code type}.
4200      * That is, if the target is exactly of the given {@code type}, it will behave
4201      * like {@code invokeExact}; otherwise it behave as if {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}
4202      * is used to convert the target to the required {@code type}.
4203      * <p>
4204      * The type of the returned invoker will not be the given {@code type}, but rather
4205      * will have all parameters except the first {@code leadingArgCount}
4206      * replaced by a single array of type {@code Object[]}, which will be
4207      * the final parameter.
4208      * <p>
4209      * Before invoking its target, the invoker will spread the final array, apply
4210      * reference casts as necessary, and unbox and widen primitive arguments.
4211      * If, when the invoker is called, the supplied array argument does
4212      * not have the correct number of elements, the invoker will throw
4213      * an {@link IllegalArgumentException} instead of invoking the target.
4214      * <p>
4215      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4216      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4217 MethodHandle invoker = MethodHandles.invoker(type);
4218 int spreadArgCount = type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount;
4219 invoker = invoker.asSpreader(Object[].class, spreadArgCount);
4220 return invoker;
4221      * }</pre></blockquote>
4222      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4223      * @param type the desired target type
4224      * @param leadingArgCount number of fixed arguments, to be passed unchanged to the target
4225      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4226      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code type} is null
4227      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code leadingArgCount} is not in
4228      *                  the range from 0 to {@code type.parameterCount()} inclusive,
4229      *                  or if the resulting method handle's type would have
4230      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4231      */
4232     public static MethodHandle spreadInvoker(MethodType type, int leadingArgCount) {
4233         if (leadingArgCount < 0 || leadingArgCount > type.parameterCount())
4234             throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad argument count", leadingArgCount);
4235         type = type.asSpreaderType(Object[].class, leadingArgCount, type.parameterCount() - leadingArgCount);
4236         return type.invokers().spreadInvoker(leadingArgCount);
4237     }
4238 
4239     /**
4240      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4241      * invoke any method handle of the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invokeExact invokeExact}.
4242      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4243      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4244      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4245      * <p>
4246      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4247      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invokeExact", type)}
4248      *
4249      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4250      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4251      * Invoker method handles can be useful when working with variable method handles
4252      * of unknown types.
4253      * For example, to emulate an {@code invokeExact} call to a variable method
4254      * handle {@code M}, extract its type {@code T},
4255      * look up the invoker method {@code X} for {@code T},
4256      * and call the invoker method, as {@code X.invoke(T, A...)}.
4257      * (It would not work to call {@code X.invokeExact}, since the type {@code T}
4258      * is unknown.)
4259      * If spreading, collecting, or other argument transformations are required,
4260      * they can be applied once to the invoker {@code X} and reused on many {@code M}
4261      * method handle values, as long as they are compatible with the type of {@code X}.
4262      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4263      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4264      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4265      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4266      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4267      * <p>
4268      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4269      * @param type the desired target type
4270      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle of the given type
4271      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4272      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4273      */
4274     public static MethodHandle exactInvoker(MethodType type) {
4275         return type.invokers().exactInvoker();
4276     }
4277 
4278     /**
4279      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4280      * invoke any method handle compatible with the given type, as if by {@link MethodHandle#invoke invoke}.
4281      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is
4282      * exactly equal to the desired type, except that it will accept
4283      * an additional leading argument of type {@code MethodHandle}.
4284      * <p>
4285      * Before invoking its target, if the target differs from the expected type,
4286      * the invoker will apply reference casts as
4287      * necessary and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4288      * Similarly, the return value will be converted as necessary.
4289      * If the target is a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector variable arity method handle},
4290      * the required arity conversion will be made, again as if by {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.
4291      * <p>
4292      * This method is equivalent to the following code (though it may be more efficient):
4293      * {@code publicLookup().findVirtual(MethodHandle.class, "invoke", type)}
4294      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4295      * <em>Discussion:</em>
4296      * A {@linkplain MethodType#genericMethodType general method type} is one which
4297      * mentions only {@code Object} arguments and return values.
4298      * An invoker for such a type is capable of calling any method handle
4299      * of the same arity as the general type.
4300      * <p style="font-size:smaller;">
4301      * <em>(Note:  The invoker method is not available via the Core Reflection API.
4302      * An attempt to call {@linkplain java.lang.reflect.Method#invoke java.lang.reflect.Method.invoke}
4303      * on the declared {@code invokeExact} or {@code invoke} method will raise an
4304      * {@link java.lang.UnsupportedOperationException UnsupportedOperationException}.)</em>
4305      * <p>
4306      * This method throws no reflective or security exceptions.
4307      * @param type the desired target type
4308      * @return a method handle suitable for invoking any method handle convertible to the given type
4309      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the resulting method handle's type would have
4310      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4311      */
4312     public static MethodHandle invoker(MethodType type) {
4313         return type.invokers().genericInvoker();
4314     }

4316     /**

4320      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4321      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4322      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.

4327      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is of the given type.
4328      * @since 9
4329      */
4330     public static MethodHandle varHandleExactInvoker(VarHandle.AccessMode accessMode, MethodType type) {

4334     /**
4335      * Produces a special <em>invoker method handle</em> which can be used to
4336      * invoke a signature-polymorphic access mode method on any VarHandle whose
4337      * associated access mode type is compatible with the given type.
4338      * The resulting invoker will have a type which is exactly equal to the
4339      * desired given type, except that it will accept an additional leading
4340      * argument of type {@code VarHandle}.
4341      * <p>
4342      * Before invoking its target, if the access mode type differs from the
4343      * desired given type, the invoker will apply reference casts as necessary
4344      * and box, unbox, or widen primitive values, as if by
4345      * {@link MethodHandle#asType asType}.  Similarly, the return value will be
4346      * converted as necessary.
4347      * <p>

4350      *

4354      *         any VarHandle whose access mode type is convertible to the given
4355      *         type.

4366 
4367      /// method handle modification (creation from other method handles)
4368 
4369     /**
4370      * Produces a method handle which adapts the type of the
4371      * given method handle to a new type by pairwise argument and return type conversion.
4372      * The original type and new type must have the same number of arguments.
4373      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4374      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4375      * <p>
4376      * If the original type and new type are equal, returns target.
4377      * <p>
4378      * The same conversions are allowed as for {@link MethodHandle#asType MethodHandle.asType},
4379      * and some additional conversions are also applied if those conversions fail.
4380      * Given types <em>T0</em>, <em>T1</em>, one of the following conversions is applied
4381      * if possible, before or instead of any conversions done by {@code asType}:
4382      * <ul>
4383      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are references, and <em>T1</em> is an interface type,
4384      *     then the value of type <em>T0</em> is passed as a <em>T1</em> without a cast.
4385      *     (This treatment of interfaces follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4386      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is boolean and <em>T1</em> is another primitive,
4387      *     the boolean is converted to a byte value, 1 for true, 0 for false.
4388      *     (This treatment follows the usage of the bytecode verifier.)
4389      * <li>If <em>T1</em> is boolean and <em>T0</em> is another primitive,
4390      *     <em>T0</em> is converted to byte via Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5),
4391      *     and the low order bit of the result is tested, as if by {@code (x & 1) != 0}.
4392      * <li>If <em>T0</em> and <em>T1</em> are primitives other than boolean,
4393      *     then a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) is applied.
4394      *     (Specifically, <em>T0</em> will convert to <em>T1</em> by
4395      *     widening and/or narrowing.)
4396      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive, an unboxing
4397      *     conversion will be applied at runtime, possibly followed
4398      *     by a Java casting conversion (JLS 5.5) on the primitive value,
4399      *     possibly followed by a conversion from byte to boolean by testing
4400      *     the low-order bit.
4401      * <li>If <em>T0</em> is a reference and <em>T1</em> a primitive,
4402      *     and if the reference is null at runtime, a zero value is introduced.
4403      * </ul>
4404      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are retyped
4405      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4406      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after performing
4407      *           any necessary argument conversions, and arranges for any
4408      *           necessary return value conversions
4409      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
4410      * @throws WrongMethodTypeException if the conversion cannot be made
4411      * @see MethodHandle#asType
4412      */
4413     public static MethodHandle explicitCastArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4414         explicitCastArgumentsChecks(target, newType);
4415         // use the asTypeCache when possible:
4416         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4417         if (oldType == newType)  return target;
4418         if (oldType.explicitCastEquivalentToAsType(newType)) {
4419             return target.asFixedArity().asType(newType);
4420         }
4421         return MethodHandleImpl.makePairwiseConvert(target, newType, false);
4422     }
4423 
4424     private static void explicitCastArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType) {
4425         if (target.type().parameterCount() != newType.parameterCount()) {
4426             throw new WrongMethodTypeException("cannot explicitly cast " + target + " to " + newType);
4427         }
4428     }
4429 
4430     /**
4431      * Produces a method handle which adapts the calling sequence of the
4432      * given method handle to a new type, by reordering the arguments.
4433      * The resulting method handle is guaranteed to report a type
4434      * which is equal to the desired new type.
4435      * <p>
4436      * The given array controls the reordering.
4437      * Call {@code #I} the number of incoming parameters (the value
4438      * {@code newType.parameterCount()}, and call {@code #O} the number
4439      * of outgoing parameters (the value {@code target.type().parameterCount()}).
4440      * Then the length of the reordering array must be {@code #O},
4441      * and each element must be a non-negative number less than {@code #I}.
4442      * For every {@code N} less than {@code #O}, the {@code N}-th
4443      * outgoing argument will be taken from the {@code I}-th incoming
4444      * argument, where {@code I} is {@code reorder[N]}.
4445      * <p>
4446      * No argument or return value conversions are applied.
4447      * The type of each incoming argument, as determined by {@code newType},
4448      * must be identical to the type of the corresponding outgoing parameter
4449      * or parameters in the target method handle.
4450      * The return type of {@code newType} must be identical to the return
4451      * type of the original target.
4452      * <p>
4453      * The reordering array need not specify an actual permutation.
4454      * An incoming argument will be duplicated if its index appears
4455      * more than once in the array, and an incoming argument will be dropped
4456      * if its index does not appear in the array.
4457      * As in the case of {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments},
4458      * incoming arguments which are not mentioned in the reordering array
4459      * may be of any type, as determined only by {@code newType}.
4460      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4461 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4462 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4463 ...
4464 MethodType intfn1 = methodType(int.class, int.class);
4465 MethodType intfn2 = methodType(int.class, int.class, int.class);
4466 MethodHandle sub = ... (int x, int y) -> (x-y) ...;
4467 assert(sub.type().equals(intfn2));
4468 MethodHandle sub1 = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 0, 1);
4469 MethodHandle rsub = permuteArguments(sub, intfn2, 1, 0);
4470 assert((int)rsub.invokeExact(1, 100) == 99);
4471 MethodHandle add = ... (int x, int y) -> (x+y) ...;
4472 assert(add.type().equals(intfn2));
4473 MethodHandle twice = permuteArguments(add, intfn1, 0, 0);
4474 assert(twice.type().equals(intfn1));
4475 assert((int)twice.invokeExact(21) == 42);
4476      * }</pre></blockquote>
4477      * <p>
4478      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4479      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4480      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are reordered
4481      * @param newType the expected type of the new method handle
4482      * @param reorder an index array which controls the reordering
4483      * @return a method handle which delegates to the target after it
4484      *           drops unused arguments and moves and/or duplicates the other arguments
4485      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
4486      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the index array length is not equal to
4487      *                  the arity of the target, or if any index array element
4488      *                  not a valid index for a parameter of {@code newType},
4489      *                  or if two corresponding parameter types in
4490      *                  {@code target.type()} and {@code newType} are not identical,
4491      */
4492     public static MethodHandle permuteArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodType newType, int... reorder) {
4493         reorder = reorder.clone();  // get a private copy
4494         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4495         permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType);
4496         // first detect dropped arguments and handle them separately
4497         int[] originalReorder = reorder;
4498         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4499         LambdaForm form = result.form;
4500         int newArity = newType.parameterCount();
4501         // Normalize the reordering into a real permutation,
4502         // by removing duplicates and adding dropped elements.
4503         // This somewhat improves lambda form caching, as well
4504         // as simplifying the transform by breaking it up into steps.
4505         for (int ddIdx; (ddIdx = findFirstDupOrDrop(reorder, newArity)) != 0; ) {
4506             if (ddIdx > 0) {
4507                 // We found a duplicated entry at reorder[ddIdx].
4508                 // Example:  (x,y,z)->asList(x,y,z)
4509                 // permuted by [1*,0,1] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a1,a0,a1)
4510                 // permuted by [0,1,0*] => (a0,a1)=>asList(a0,a1,a0)
4511                 // The starred element corresponds to the argument
4512                 // deleted by the dupArgumentForm transform.
4513                 int srcPos = ddIdx, dstPos = srcPos, dupVal = reorder[srcPos];
4514                 boolean killFirst = false;
4515                 for (int val; (val = reorder[--dstPos]) != dupVal; ) {
4516                     // Set killFirst if the dup is larger than an intervening position.
4517                     // This will remove at least one inversion from the permutation.
4518                     if (dupVal > val) killFirst = true;
4519                 }
4520                 if (!killFirst) {
4521                     srcPos = dstPos;
4522                     dstPos = ddIdx;
4523                 }
4524                 form = form.editor().dupArgumentForm(1 + srcPos, 1 + dstPos);
4525                 assert (reorder[srcPos] == reorder[dstPos]);
4526                 oldType = oldType.dropParameterTypes(dstPos, dstPos + 1);
4527                 // contract the reordering by removing the element at dstPos
4528                 int tailPos = dstPos + 1;
4529                 System.arraycopy(reorder, tailPos, reorder, dstPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4530                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length - 1);
4531             } else {
4532                 int dropVal = ~ddIdx, insPos = 0;
4533                 while (insPos < reorder.length && reorder[insPos] < dropVal) {
4534                     // Find first element of reorder larger than dropVal.
4535                     // This is where we will insert the dropVal.
4536                     insPos += 1;
4537                 }
4538                 Class<?> ptype = newType.parameterType(dropVal);
4539                 form = form.editor().addArgumentForm(1 + insPos, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4540                 oldType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(insPos, ptype);
4541                 // expand the reordering by inserting an element at insPos
4542                 int tailPos = insPos + 1;
4543                 reorder = Arrays.copyOf(reorder, reorder.length + 1);
4544                 System.arraycopy(reorder, insPos, reorder, tailPos, reorder.length - tailPos);
4545                 reorder[insPos] = dropVal;
4546             }
4547             assert (permuteArgumentChecks(reorder, newType, oldType));
4548         }
4549         assert (reorder.length == newArity);  // a perfect permutation
4550         // Note:  This may cache too many distinct LFs. Consider backing off to varargs code.
4551         form = form.editor().permuteArgumentsForm(1, reorder);
4552         if (newType == result.type() && form == result.internalForm())
4553             return result;
4554         return result.copyWith(newType, form);
4555     }
4556 
4557     /**
4558      * Return an indication of any duplicate or omission in reorder.
4559      * If the reorder contains a duplicate entry, return the index of the second occurrence.
4560      * Otherwise, return ~(n), for the first n in [0..newArity-1] that is not present in reorder.
4561      * Otherwise, return zero.
4562      * If an element not in [0..newArity-1] is encountered, return reorder.length.
4563      */
4564     private static int findFirstDupOrDrop(int[] reorder, int newArity) {
4565         final int BIT_LIMIT = 63;  // max number of bits in bit mask
4566         if (newArity < BIT_LIMIT) {
4567             long mask = 0;
4568             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4569                 int arg = reorder[i];
4570                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4571                     return reorder.length;
4572                 }
4573                 long bit = 1L << arg;
4574                 if ((mask & bit) != 0) {
4575                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4576                 }
4577                 mask |= bit;
4578             }
4579             if (mask == (1L << newArity) - 1) {
4580                 assert(Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(Long.lowestOneBit(~mask)) == newArity);
4581                 return 0;
4582             }
4583             // find first zero
4584             long zeroBit = Long.lowestOneBit(~mask);
4585             int zeroPos = Long.numberOfTrailingZeros(zeroBit);
4586             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4587             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4588                 return 0;
4589             }
4590             return ~zeroPos;
4591         } else {
4592             // same algorithm, different bit set
4593             BitSet mask = new BitSet(newArity);
4594             for (int i = 0; i < reorder.length; i++) {
4595                 int arg = reorder[i];
4596                 if (arg >= newArity) {
4597                     return reorder.length;
4598                 }
4599                 if (mask.get(arg)) {
4600                     return i;  // >0 indicates a dup
4601                 }
4602                 mask.set(arg);
4603             }
4604             int zeroPos = mask.nextClearBit(0);
4605             assert(zeroPos <= newArity);
4606             if (zeroPos == newArity) {
4607                 return 0;
4608             }
4609             return ~zeroPos;
4610         }
4611     }
4612 
4613     static boolean permuteArgumentChecks(int[] reorder, MethodType newType, MethodType oldType) {
4614         if (newType.returnType() != oldType.returnType())
4615             throw newIllegalArgumentException("return types do not match",
4616                     oldType, newType);
4617         if (reorder.length == oldType.parameterCount()) {
4618             int limit = newType.parameterCount();
4619             boolean bad = false;
4620             for (int j = 0; j < reorder.length; j++) {
4621                 int i = reorder[j];
4622                 if (i < 0 || i >= limit) {
4623                     bad = true; break;
4624                 }
4625                 Class<?> src = newType.parameterType(i);
4626                 Class<?> dst = oldType.parameterType(j);
4627                 if (src != dst)
4628                     throw newIllegalArgumentException("parameter types do not match after reorder",
4629                             oldType, newType);
4630             }
4631             if (!bad)  return true;
4632         }
4633         throw newIllegalArgumentException("bad reorder array: "+Arrays.toString(reorder));
4634     }
4635 
4636     /**
4637      * Produces a method handle of the requested return type which returns the given
4638      * constant value every time it is invoked.
4639      * <p>
4640      * Before the method handle is returned, the passed-in value is converted to the requested type.
4641      * If the requested type is primitive, widening primitive conversions are attempted,
4642      * else reference conversions are attempted.
4643      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code identity(type).bindTo(value)}.
4644      * @param type the return type of the desired method handle
4645      * @param value the value to return
4646      * @return a method handle of the given return type and no arguments, which always returns the given value
4647      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code type} argument is null
4648      * @throws ClassCastException if the value cannot be converted to the required return type
4649      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4650      */
4651     public static MethodHandle constant(Class<?> type, Object value) {
4652         if (type.isPrimitive()) {
4653             if (type == void.class)
4654                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("void type");
4655             Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type);
4656             value = w.convert(value, type);
4657             if (w.zero().equals(value))
4658                 return zero(w, type);
4659             return insertArguments(identity(type), 0, value);
4660         } else {
4661             if (value == null)
4662                 return zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4663             return identity(type).bindTo(value);
4664         }
4665     }
4666 
4667     /**
4668      * Produces a method handle which returns its sole argument when invoked.
4669      * @param type the type of the sole parameter and return value of the desired method handle
4670      * @return a unary method handle which accepts and returns the given type
4671      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4672      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the given type is {@code void.class}
4673      */
4674     public static MethodHandle identity(Class<?> type) {
4675         Wrapper btw = (type.isPrimitive() ? Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type) : Wrapper.OBJECT);
4676         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4677         MethodHandle ident = IDENTITY_MHS[pos];
4678         if (ident == null) {
4679             ident = setCachedMethodHandle(IDENTITY_MHS, pos, makeIdentity(btw.primitiveType()));
4680         }
4681         if (ident.type().returnType() == type)
4682             return ident;
4683         // something like identity(Foo.class); do not bother to intern these
4684         assert (btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4685         return makeIdentity(type);
4686     }
4687 
4688     /**
4689      * Produces a constant method handle of the requested return type which
4690      * returns the default value for that type every time it is invoked.
4691      * The resulting constant method handle will have no side effects.
4692      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to {@code empty(methodType(type))}.
4693      * It is also equivalent to {@code explicitCastArguments(constant(Object.class, null), methodType(type))},
4694      * since {@code explicitCastArguments} converts {@code null} to default values.
4695      * @param type the expected return type of the desired method handle
4696      * @return a constant method handle that takes no arguments
4697      *         and returns the default value of the given type (or void, if the type is void)
4698      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4699      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4700      * @see MethodHandles#empty
4701      * @see MethodHandles#explicitCastArguments
4702      * @since 9
4703      */
4704     public static MethodHandle zero(Class<?> type) {
4705         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4706         return type.isPrimitive() ?  zero(Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(type), type) : zero(Wrapper.OBJECT, type);
4707     }
4708 
4709     private static MethodHandle identityOrVoid(Class<?> type) {
4710         return type == void.class ? zero(type) : identity(type);
4711     }
4712 
4713     /**
4714      * Produces a method handle of the requested type which ignores any arguments, does nothing,
4715      * and returns a suitable default depending on the return type.
4716      * That is, it returns a zero primitive value, a {@code null}, or {@code void}.
4717      * <p>The returned method handle is equivalent to
4718      * {@code dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList())}.
4719      *
4720      * @apiNote Given a predicate and target, a useful "if-then" construct can be produced as
4721      * {@code guardWithTest(pred, target, empty(target.type())}.
4722      * @param type the type of the desired method handle
4723      * @return a constant method handle of the given type, which returns a default value of the given return type
4724      * @throws NullPointerException if the argument is null
4725      * @see MethodHandles#zero
4726      * @see MethodHandles#constant
4727      * @since 9
4728      */
4729     public static  MethodHandle empty(MethodType type) {
4730         Objects.requireNonNull(type);
4731         return dropArguments(zero(type.returnType()), 0, type.parameterList());
4732     }
4733 
4734     private static final MethodHandle[] IDENTITY_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4735     private static MethodHandle makeIdentity(Class<?> ptype) {
4736         MethodType mtype = methodType(ptype, ptype);
4737         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.identityForm(BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4738         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.IDENTITY);
4739     }
4740 
4741     private static MethodHandle zero(Wrapper btw, Class<?> rtype) {
4742         int pos = btw.ordinal();
4743         MethodHandle zero = ZERO_MHS[pos];
4744         if (zero == null) {
4745             zero = setCachedMethodHandle(ZERO_MHS, pos, makeZero(btw.primitiveType()));
4746         }
4747         if (zero.type().returnType() == rtype)
4748             return zero;
4749         assert(btw == Wrapper.OBJECT);
4750         return makeZero(rtype);
4751     }
