4752     private static final MethodHandle[] ZERO_MHS = new MethodHandle[Wrapper.COUNT];
4753     private static MethodHandle makeZero(Class<?> rtype) {
4754         MethodType mtype = methodType(rtype);
4755         LambdaForm lform = LambdaForm.zeroForm(BasicType.basicType(rtype));
4756         return MethodHandleImpl.makeIntrinsic(mtype, lform, Intrinsic.ZERO);
4757     }
4758 
4759     private static synchronized MethodHandle setCachedMethodHandle(MethodHandle[] cache, int pos, MethodHandle value) {
4760         // Simulate a CAS, to avoid racy duplication of results.
4761         MethodHandle prev = cache[pos];
4762         if (prev != null) return prev;
4763         return cache[pos] = value;
4764     }
4765 
4766     /**
4767      * Provides a target method handle with one or more <em>bound arguments</em>
4768      * in advance of the method handle's invocation.
4769      * The formal parameters to the target corresponding to the bound
4770      * arguments are called <em>bound parameters</em>.
4771      * Returns a new method handle which saves away the bound arguments.
4772      * When it is invoked, it receives arguments for any non-bound parameters,
4773      * binds the saved arguments to their corresponding parameters,
4774      * and calls the original target.
4775      * <p>
4776      * The type of the new method handle will drop the types for the bound
4777      * parameters from the original target type, since the new method handle
4778      * will no longer require those arguments to be supplied by its callers.
4779      * <p>
4780      * Each given argument object must match the corresponding bound parameter type.
4781      * If a bound parameter type is a primitive, the argument object
4782      * must be a wrapper, and will be unboxed to produce the primitive value.
4783      * <p>
4784      * The {@code pos} argument selects which parameters are to be bound.
4785      * It may range between zero and <i>N-L</i> (inclusively),
4786      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target method handle
4787      * and <i>L</i> is the length of the values array.
4788      * <p>
4789      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
4790      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
4791      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the argument is inserted
4792      * @param pos where to insert the argument (zero for the first)
4793      * @param values the series of arguments to insert
4794      * @return a method handle which inserts an additional argument,
4795      *         before calling the original method handle
4796      * @throws NullPointerException if the target or the {@code values} array is null
4797      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if (@code pos) is less than {@code 0} or greater than
4798      *         {@code N - L} where {@code N} is the arity of the target method handle and {@code L}
4799      *         is the length of the values array.
4800      * @throws ClassCastException if an argument does not match the corresponding bound parameter
4801      *         type.
4802      * @see MethodHandle#bindTo
4803      */
4804     public static MethodHandle insertArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Object... values) {
4805         int insCount = values.length;
4806         Class<?>[] ptypes = insertArgumentsChecks(target, insCount, pos);
4807         if (insCount == 0)  return target;
4808         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4809         for (int i = 0; i < insCount; i++) {
4810             Object value = values[i];
4811             Class<?> ptype = ptypes[pos+i];
4812             if (ptype.isPrimitive()) {
4813                 result = insertArgumentPrimitive(result, pos, ptype, value);
4814             } else {
4815                 value = ptype.cast(value);  // throw CCE if needed
4816                 result = result.bindArgumentL(pos, value);
4817             }
4818         }
4819         return result;
4820     }
4821 
4822     private static BoundMethodHandle insertArgumentPrimitive(BoundMethodHandle result, int pos,
4823                                                              Class<?> ptype, Object value) {
4824         Wrapper w = Wrapper.forPrimitiveType(ptype);
4825         // perform unboxing and/or primitive conversion
4826         value = w.convert(value, ptype);
4827         switch (w) {
4828         case INT:     return result.bindArgumentI(pos, (int)value);
4829         case LONG:    return result.bindArgumentJ(pos, (long)value);
4830         case FLOAT:   return result.bindArgumentF(pos, (float)value);
4831         case DOUBLE:  return result.bindArgumentD(pos, (double)value);
4832         default:      return result.bindArgumentI(pos, ValueConversions.widenSubword(value));
4833         }
4834     }
4835 
4836     private static Class<?>[] insertArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int insCount, int pos) throws RuntimeException {
4837         MethodType oldType = target.type();
4838         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4839         int inargs  = outargs - insCount;
4840         if (inargs < 0)
4841             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many values to insert");
4842         if (pos < 0 || pos > inargs)
4843             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to append");
4844         return oldType.ptypes();
4845     }
4846 
4847     /**
4848      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4849      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4850      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4851      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4852      * at some given position.
4853      * <p>
4854      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4855      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4856      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4857      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4858      * they will come after.
4859      * <p>
4860      * <b>Example:</b>
4861      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4862 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4863 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4864 ...
4865 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4866   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4867 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4868 MethodType bigType = cat.type().insertParameterTypes(0, int.class, String.class);
4869 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, bigType.parameterList().subList(0,2));
4870 assertEquals(bigType, d0.type());
4871 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact(123, "x", "y", "z"));
4872      * }</pre></blockquote>
4873      * <p>
4874      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4875      * <blockquote><pre>
4876      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,Class...) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, valueTypes.toArray(new Class[0]))}
4877      * </pre></blockquote>
4878      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4879      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4880      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4881      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4882      *         before calling the original method handle
4883      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4884      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} list or any of its elements is null
4885      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4886      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4887      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have too many parameters
4888      */
4889     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4890         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes.toArray()));
4891     }
4892 
4893     private static List<Class<?>> copyTypes(Object[] array) {
4894         return Arrays.asList(Arrays.copyOf(array, array.length, Class[].class));
4895     }
4896 
4897     private static MethodHandle dropArguments0(MethodHandle target, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4898         MethodType oldType = target.type();  // get NPE
4899         int dropped = dropArgumentChecks(oldType, pos, valueTypes);
4900         MethodType newType = oldType.insertParameterTypes(pos, valueTypes);
4901         if (dropped == 0)  return target;
4902         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
4903         LambdaForm lform = result.form;
4904         int insertFormArg = 1 + pos;
4905         for (Class<?> ptype : valueTypes) {
4906             lform = lform.editor().addArgumentForm(insertFormArg++, BasicType.basicType(ptype));
4907         }
4908         result = result.copyWith(newType, lform);
4909         return result;
4910     }
4911 
4912     private static int dropArgumentChecks(MethodType oldType, int pos, List<Class<?>> valueTypes) {
4913         int dropped = valueTypes.size();
4914         MethodType.checkSlotCount(dropped);
4915         int outargs = oldType.parameterCount();
4916         int inargs  = outargs + dropped;
4917         if (pos < 0 || pos > outargs)
4918             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no argument type to remove"
4919                     + Arrays.asList(oldType, pos, valueTypes, inargs, outargs)
4920                     );
4921         return dropped;
4922     }
4923 
4924     /**
4925      * Produces a method handle which will discard some dummy arguments
4926      * before calling some other specified <i>target</i> method handle.
4927      * The type of the new method handle will be the same as the target's type,
4928      * except it will also include the dummy argument types,
4929      * at some given position.
4930      * <p>
4931      * The {@code pos} argument may range between zero and <i>N</i>,
4932      * where <i>N</i> is the arity of the target.
4933      * If {@code pos} is zero, the dummy arguments will precede
4934      * the target's real arguments; if {@code pos} is <i>N</i>
4935      * they will come after.
4936      * @apiNote
4937      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
4938 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
4939 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
4940 ...
4941 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
4942   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
4943 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
4944 MethodHandle d0 = dropArguments(cat, 0, String.class);
4945 assertEquals("yz", (String) d0.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4946 MethodHandle d1 = dropArguments(cat, 1, String.class);
4947 assertEquals("xz", (String) d1.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4948 MethodHandle d2 = dropArguments(cat, 2, String.class);
4949 assertEquals("xy", (String) d2.invokeExact("x", "y", "z"));
4950 MethodHandle d12 = dropArguments(cat, 1, int.class, boolean.class);
4951 assertEquals("xz", (String) d12.invokeExact("x", 12, true, "z"));
4952      * }</pre></blockquote>
4953      * <p>
4954      * This method is also equivalent to the following code:
4955      * <blockquote><pre>
4956      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments}{@code (target, pos, Arrays.asList(valueTypes))}
4957      * </pre></blockquote>
4958      * @param target the method handle to invoke after the arguments are dropped
4959      * @param pos position of first argument to drop (zero for the leftmost)
4960      * @param valueTypes the type(s) of the argument(s) to drop
4961      * @return a method handle which drops arguments of the given types,
4962      *         before calling the original method handle
4963      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null,
4964      *                              or if the {@code valueTypes} array or any of its elements is null
4965      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code valueTypes} is {@code void.class},
4966      *                  or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
4967      *                  or if the new method handle's type would have
4968      *                  <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
4969      */
4970     public static MethodHandle dropArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, Class<?>... valueTypes) {
4971         return dropArguments0(target, pos, copyTypes(valueTypes));
4972     }
4973 
4974     // private version which allows caller some freedom with error handling
4975     private static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos,
4976                                       boolean nullOnFailure) {
4977         newTypes = copyTypes(newTypes.toArray());
4978         List<Class<?>> oldTypes = target.type().parameterList();
4979         int match = oldTypes.size();
4980         if (skip != 0) {
4981             if (skip < 0 || skip > match) {
4982                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal skip", skip, target);
4983             }
4984             oldTypes = oldTypes.subList(skip, match);
4985             match -= skip;
4986         }
4987         List<Class<?>> addTypes = newTypes;
4988         int add = addTypes.size();
4989         if (pos != 0) {
4990             if (pos < 0 || pos > add) {
4991                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("illegal pos", pos, newTypes);
4992             }
4993             addTypes = addTypes.subList(pos, add);
4994             add -= pos;
4995             assert(addTypes.size() == add);
4996         }
4997         // Do not add types which already match the existing arguments.
4998         if (match > add || !oldTypes.equals(addTypes.subList(0, match))) {
4999             if (nullOnFailure) {
5000                 return null;
5001             }
5002             throw newIllegalArgumentException("argument lists do not match", oldTypes, newTypes);
5003         }
5004         addTypes = addTypes.subList(match, add);
5005         add -= match;
5006         assert(addTypes.size() == add);
5007         // newTypes:     (   P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5008         // target: ( S*[skip],        M*[match]  )
5009         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5010         if (add > 0) {
5011             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip+ match, addTypes);
5012         }
5013         // adapter: (S*[skip],        M*[match], A*[add] )
5014         if (pos > 0) {
5015             adapter = dropArguments0(adapter, skip, newTypes.subList(0, pos));
5016         }
5017         // adapter: (S*[skip], P*[pos], M*[match], A*[add] )
5018         return adapter;
5019     }
5020 
5021     /**
5022      * Adapts a target method handle to match the given parameter type list. If necessary, adds dummy arguments. Some
5023      * leading parameters can be skipped before matching begins. The remaining types in the {@code target}'s parameter
5024      * type list must be a sub-list of the {@code newTypes} type list at the starting position {@code pos}. The
5025      * resulting handle will have the target handle's parameter type list, with any non-matching parameter types (before
5026      * or after the matching sub-list) inserted in corresponding positions of the target's original parameters, as if by
5027      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5028      * <p>
5029      * The resulting handle will have the same return type as the target handle.
5030      * <p>
5031      * In more formal terms, assume these two type lists:<ul>
5032      * <li>The target handle has the parameter type list {@code S..., M...}, with as many types in {@code S} as
5033      * indicated by {@code skip}. The {@code M} types are those that are supposed to match part of the given type list,
5034      * {@code newTypes}.
5035      * <li>The {@code newTypes} list contains types {@code P..., M..., A...}, with as many types in {@code P} as
5036      * indicated by {@code pos}. The {@code M} types are precisely those that the {@code M} types in the target handle's
5037      * parameter type list are supposed to match. The types in {@code A} are additional types found after the matching
5038      * sub-list.
5039      * </ul>
5040      * Given these assumptions, the result of an invocation of {@code dropArgumentsToMatch} will have the parameter type
5041      * list {@code S..., P..., M..., A...}, with the {@code P} and {@code A} types inserted as if by
5042      * {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle, int, Class[])}.
5043      *
5044      * @apiNote
5045      * Two method handles whose argument lists are "effectively identical" (i.e., identical in a common prefix) may be
5046      * mutually converted to a common type by two calls to {@code dropArgumentsToMatch}, as follows:
5047      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5048 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5049 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5050 ...
5051 ...
5052 MethodHandle h0 = constant(boolean.class, true);
5053 MethodHandle h1 = lookup().findVirtual(String.class, "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5054 MethodType bigType = h1.type().insertParameterTypes(1, String.class, int.class);
5055 MethodHandle h2 = dropArguments(h1, 0, bigType.parameterList());
5056 if (h1.type().parameterCount() < h2.type().parameterCount())
5057     h1 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h1, 0, h2.type().parameterList(), 0);  // lengthen h1
5058 else
5059     h2 = dropArgumentsToMatch(h2, 0, h1.type().parameterList(), 0);    // lengthen h2
5060 MethodHandle h3 = guardWithTest(h0, h1, h2);
5061 assertEquals("xy", h3.invoke("x", "y", 1, "a", "b", "c"));
5062      * }</pre></blockquote>
5063      * @param target the method handle to adapt
5064      * @param skip number of targets parameters to disregard (they will be unchanged)
5065      * @param newTypes the list of types to match {@code target}'s parameter type list to
5066      * @param pos place in {@code newTypes} where the non-skipped target parameters must occur
5067      * @return a possibly adapted method handle
5068      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5069      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any element of {@code newTypes} is {@code void.class},
5070      *         or if {@code skip} is negative or greater than the arity of the target,
5071      *         or if {@code pos} is negative or greater than the newTypes list size,
5072      *         or if {@code newTypes} does not contain the {@code target}'s non-skipped parameter types at position
5073      *         {@code pos}.
5074      * @since 9
5075      */
5076     public static MethodHandle dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle target, int skip, List<Class<?>> newTypes, int pos) {
5077         Objects.requireNonNull(target);
5078         Objects.requireNonNull(newTypes);
5079         return dropArgumentsToMatch(target, skip, newTypes, pos, false);
5080     }
5081 
5082     /**
5083      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5084      * one or more of its arguments, each with its own unary filter function,
5085      * and then calling the target with each pre-processed argument
5086      * replaced by the result of its corresponding filter function.
5087      * <p>
5088      * The pre-processing is performed by one or more method handles,
5089      * specified in the elements of the {@code filters} array.
5090      * The first element of the filter array corresponds to the {@code pos}
5091      * argument of the target, and so on in sequence.
5092      * The filter functions are invoked in left to right order.
5093      * <p>
5094      * Null arguments in the array are treated as identity functions,
5095      * and the corresponding arguments left unchanged.
5096      * (If there are no non-null elements in the array, the original target is returned.)
5097      * Each filter is applied to the corresponding argument of the adapter.
5098      * <p>
5099      * If a filter {@code F} applies to the {@code N}th argument of
5100      * the target, then {@code F} must be a method handle which
5101      * takes exactly one argument.  The type of {@code F}'s sole argument
5102      * replaces the corresponding argument type of the target
5103      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5104      * The return type of {@code F} must be identical to the corresponding
5105      * parameter type of the target.
5106      * <p>
5107      * It is an error if there are elements of {@code filters}
5108      * (null or not)
5109      * which do not correspond to argument positions in the target.
5110      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5111      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5112 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5113 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5114 ...
5115 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5116   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5117 MethodHandle upcase = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5118   "toUpperCase", methodType(String.class));
5119 assertEquals("xy", (String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y"));
5120 MethodHandle f0 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase);
5121 assertEquals("Xy", (String) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // Xy
5122 MethodHandle f1 = filterArguments(cat, 1, upcase);
5123 assertEquals("xY", (String) f1.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xY
5124 MethodHandle f2 = filterArguments(cat, 0, upcase, upcase);
5125 assertEquals("XY", (String) f2.invokeExact("x", "y")); // XY
5126      * }</pre></blockquote>
5127      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5128      * denotes the return type of both the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5129      * {@code P}/{@code p} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values
5130      * of the parameters and arguments that precede and follow the filter position
5131      * {@code pos}, respectively. {@code A[i]}/{@code a[i]} stand for the types and
5132      * values of the filtered parameters and arguments; they also represent the
5133      * return types of the {@code filter[i]} handles. The latter accept arguments
5134      * {@code v[i]} of type {@code V[i]}, which also appear in the signature of
5135      * the resulting adapter.
5136      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5137      * T target(P... p, A[i]... a[i], B... b);
5138      * A[i] filter[i](V[i]);
5139      * T adapter(P... p, V[i]... v[i], B... b) {
5140      *   return target(p..., filter[i](v[i])..., b...);
5141      * }
5142      * }</pre></blockquote>
5143      * <p>
5144      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5145      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5146      *
5147      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are filtered
5148      * @param pos the position of the first argument to filter
5149      * @param filters method handles to call initially on filtered arguments
5150      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument filtering logic
5151      * @throws NullPointerException if the target is null
5152      *                              or if the {@code filters} array is null
5153      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if a non-null element of {@code filters}
5154      *          does not match a corresponding argument type of target as described above,
5155      *          or if the {@code pos+filters.length} is greater than {@code target.type().parameterCount()},
5156      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5157      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5158      */
5159     public static MethodHandle filterArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle... filters) {
5160         // In method types arguments start at index 0, while the LF
5161         // editor have the MH receiver at position 0 - adjust appropriately.
5162         final int MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET = 1;
5163         filterArgumentsCheckArity(target, pos, filters);
5164         MethodHandle adapter = target;
5165 
5166         // keep track of currently matched filters, as to optimize repeated filters
5167         int index = 0;
5168         int[] positions = new int[filters.length];
5169         MethodHandle filter = null;
5170 
5171         // process filters in reverse order so that the invocation of
5172         // the resulting adapter will invoke the filters in left-to-right order
5173         for (int i = filters.length - 1; i >= 0; --i) {
5174             MethodHandle newFilter = filters[i];
5175             if (newFilter == null) continue;  // ignore null elements of filters
5176 
5177             // flush changes on update
5178             if (filter != newFilter) {
5179                 if (filter != null) {
5180                     if (index > 1) {
5181                         adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5182                     } else {
5183                         adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5184                     }
5185                 }
5186                 filter = newFilter;
5187                 index = 0;
5188             }
5189 
5190             filterArgumentChecks(target, pos + i, newFilter);
5191             positions[index++] = pos + i + MH_RECEIVER_OFFSET;
5192         }
5193         if (index > 1) {
5194             adapter = filterRepeatedArgument(adapter, filter, Arrays.copyOf(positions, index));
5195         } else if (index == 1) {
5196             adapter = filterArgument(adapter, positions[0] - 1, filter);
5197         }
5198         return adapter;
5199     }
5200 
5201     private static MethodHandle filterRepeatedArgument(MethodHandle adapter, MethodHandle filter, int[] positions) {
5202         MethodType targetType = adapter.type();
5203         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5204         BoundMethodHandle result = adapter.rebind();
5205         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5206 
5207         Class<?>[] ptypes = targetType.ptypes().clone();
5208         for (int pos : positions) {
5209             ptypes[pos - 1] = newParamType;
5210         }
5211         MethodType newType = MethodType.makeImpl(targetType.rtype(), ptypes, true);
5212 
5213         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterRepeatedArgumentForm(BasicType.basicType(newParamType), positions);
5214         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5215     }
5216 
5217     /*non-public*/
5218     static MethodHandle filterArgument(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5219         filterArgumentChecks(target, pos, filter);
5220         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5221         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5222         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5223         Class<?> newParamType = filterType.parameterType(0);
5224         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterArgumentForm(1 + pos, BasicType.basicType(newParamType));
5225         MethodType newType = targetType.changeParameterType(pos, newParamType);
5226         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5227         return result;
5228     }
5229 
5230     private static void filterArgumentsCheckArity(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle[] filters) {
5231         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5232         int maxPos = targetType.parameterCount();
5233         if (pos + filters.length > maxPos)
5234             throw newIllegalArgumentException("too many filters");
5235     }
5236 
5237     private static void filterArgumentChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5238         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5239         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5240         if (filterType.parameterCount() != 1
5241             || filterType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(pos))
5242             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5243     }
5244 
5245     /**
5246      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5247      * a sub-sequence of its arguments with a filter (another method handle).
5248      * The pre-processed arguments are replaced by the result (if any) of the
5249      * filter function.
5250      * The target is then called on the modified (usually shortened) argument list.
5251      * <p>
5252      * If the filter returns a value, the target must accept that value as
5253      * its argument in position {@code pos}, preceded and/or followed by
5254      * any arguments not passed to the filter.
5255      * If the filter returns void, the target must accept all arguments
5256      * not passed to the filter.
5257      * No arguments are reordered, and a result returned from the filter
5258      * replaces (in order) the whole subsequence of arguments originally
5259      * passed to the adapter.
5260      * <p>
5261      * The argument types (if any) of the filter
5262      * replace zero or one argument types of the target, at position {@code pos},
5263      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5264      * The return type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5265      * argument type of the target at position {@code pos}, and that target argument
5266      * is supplied by the return value of the filter.
5267      * <p>
5268      * In all cases, {@code pos} must be greater than or equal to zero, and
5269      * {@code pos} must also be less than or equal to the target's arity.
5270      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5271      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5272 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5273 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5274 ...
5275 MethodHandle deepToString = publicLookup()
5276   .findStatic(Arrays.class, "deepToString", methodType(String.class, Object[].class));
5277 
5278 MethodHandle ts1 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 1);
5279 assertEquals("[strange]", (String) ts1.invokeExact("strange"));
5280 
5281 MethodHandle ts2 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 2);
5282 assertEquals("[up, down]", (String) ts2.invokeExact("up", "down"));
5283 
5284 MethodHandle ts3 = deepToString.asCollector(String[].class, 3);
5285 MethodHandle ts3_ts2 = collectArguments(ts3, 1, ts2);
5286 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], strange]",
5287              (String) ts3_ts2.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5288 
5289 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts1 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 3, ts1);
5290 assertEquals("[top, [up, down], [strange]]",
5291              (String) ts3_ts2_ts1.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange"));
5292 
5293 MethodHandle ts3_ts2_ts3 = collectArguments(ts3_ts2, 1, ts3);
5294 assertEquals("[top, [[up, down, strange], charm], bottom]",
5295              (String) ts3_ts2_ts3.invokeExact("top", "up", "down", "strange", "charm", "bottom"));
5296      * }</pre></blockquote>
5297      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5298      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5299      * {@code V}/{@code v} stand for the return type and value of the
5300      * {@code filter}, which are also found in the signature and arguments of
5301      * the {@code target}, respectively, unless {@code V} is {@code void}.
5302      * {@code A}/{@code a} and {@code C}/{@code c} represent the parameter types
5303      * and values preceding and following the collection position, {@code pos},
5304      * in the {@code target}'s signature. They also turn up in the resulting
5305      * adapter's signature and arguments, where they surround
5306      * {@code B}/{@code b}, which represent the parameter types and arguments
5307      * to the {@code filter} (if any).
5308      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5309      * T target(A...,V,C...);
5310      * V filter(B...);
5311      * T adapter(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5312      *   V v = filter(b...);
5313      *   return target(a...,v,c...);
5314      * }
5315      * // and if the filter has no arguments:
5316      * T target2(A...,V,C...);
5317      * V filter2();
5318      * T adapter2(A... a,C... c) {
5319      *   V v = filter2();
5320      *   return target2(a...,v,c...);
5321      * }
5322      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5323      * T target3(A...,C...);
5324      * void filter3(B...);
5325      * T adapter3(A... a,B... b,C... c) {
5326      *   filter3(b...);
5327      *   return target3(a...,c...);
5328      * }
5329      * }</pre></blockquote>
5330      * <p>
5331      * A collection adapter {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)} is equivalent to
5332      * one which first "folds" the affected arguments, and then drops them, in separate
5333      * steps as follows:
5334      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5335      * mh = MethodHandles.dropArguments(mh, 1, coll.type().parameterList()); //step 2
5336      * mh = MethodHandles.foldArguments(mh, coll); //step 1
5337      * }</pre></blockquote>
5338      * If the target method handle consumes no arguments besides than the result
5339      * (if any) of the filter {@code coll}, then {@code collectArguments(mh, 0, coll)}
5340      * is equivalent to {@code filterReturnValue(coll, mh)}.
5341      * If the filter method handle {@code coll} consumes one argument and produces
5342      * a non-void result, then {@code collectArguments(mh, N, coll)}
5343      * is equivalent to {@code filterArguments(mh, N, coll)}.
5344      * Other equivalences are possible but would require argument permutation.
5345      * <p>
5346      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5347      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5348      *
5349      * @param target the method handle to invoke after filtering the subsequence of arguments
5350      * @param pos the position of the first adapter argument to pass to the filter,
5351      *            and/or the target argument which receives the result of the filter
5352      * @param filter method handle to call on the subsequence of arguments
5353      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument subsequence filtering logic
5354      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5355      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the return type of {@code filter}
5356      *          is non-void and is not the same as the {@code pos} argument of the target,
5357      *          or if {@code pos} is not between 0 and the target's arity, inclusive,
5358      *          or if the resulting method handle's type would have
5359      *          <a href="MethodHandle.html#maxarity">too many parameters</a>
5360      * @see MethodHandles#foldArguments
5361      * @see MethodHandles#filterArguments
5362      * @see MethodHandles#filterReturnValue
5363      */
5364     public static MethodHandle collectArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) {
5365         MethodType newType = collectArgumentsChecks(target, pos, filter);
5366         MethodType collectorType = filter.type();
5367         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5368         LambdaForm lform;
5369         if (collectorType.returnType().isArray() && filter.intrinsicName() == Intrinsic.NEW_ARRAY) {
5370             lform = result.editor().collectArgumentArrayForm(1 + pos, filter);
5371             if (lform != null) {
5372                 return result.copyWith(newType, lform);
5373             }
5374         }
5375         lform = result.editor().collectArgumentsForm(1 + pos, collectorType.basicType());
5376         return result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5377     }
5378 
5379     private static MethodType collectArgumentsChecks(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle filter) throws RuntimeException {
5380         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5381         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5382         Class<?> rtype = filterType.returnType();
5383         List<Class<?>> filterArgs = filterType.parameterList();
5384         if (rtype == void.class) {
5385             return targetType.insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5386         }
5387         if (rtype != targetType.parameterType(pos)) {
5388             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5389         }
5390         return targetType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos+1).insertParameterTypes(pos, filterArgs);
5391     }
5392 
5393     /**
5394      * Adapts a target method handle by post-processing
5395      * its return value (if any) with a filter (another method handle).
5396      * The result of the filter is returned from the adapter.
5397      * <p>
5398      * If the target returns a value, the filter must accept that value as
5399      * its only argument.
5400      * If the target returns void, the filter must accept no arguments.
5401      * <p>
5402      * The return type of the filter
5403      * replaces the return type of the target
5404      * in the resulting adapted method handle.
5405      * The argument type of the filter (if any) must be identical to the
5406      * return type of the target.
5407      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5408      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5409 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5410 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5411 ...
5412 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5413   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5414 MethodHandle length = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5415   "length", methodType(int.class));
5416 System.out.println((String) cat.invokeExact("x", "y")); // xy
5417 MethodHandle f0 = filterReturnValue(cat, length);
5418 System.out.println((int) f0.invokeExact("x", "y")); // 2
5419      * }</pre></blockquote>
5420      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code,
5421      * {@code T}/{@code t} represent the result type and value of the
5422      * {@code target}; {@code V}, the result type of the {@code filter}; and
5423      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the parameters and arguments
5424      * of the {@code target} as well as the resulting adapter.
5425      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5426      * T target(A...);
5427      * V filter(T);
5428      * V adapter(A... a) {
5429      *   T t = target(a...);
5430      *   return filter(t);
5431      * }
5432      * // and if the target has a void return:
5433      * void target2(A...);
5434      * V filter2();
5435      * V adapter2(A... a) {
5436      *   target2(a...);
5437      *   return filter2();
5438      * }
5439      * // and if the filter has a void return:
5440      * T target3(A...);
5441      * void filter3(V);
5442      * void adapter3(A... a) {
5443      *   T t = target3(a...);
5444      *   filter3(t);
5445      * }
5446      * }</pre></blockquote>
5447      * <p>
5448      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5449      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5450      * @param target the method handle to invoke before filtering the return value
5451      * @param filter method handle to call on the return value
5452      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified return value filtering logic
5453      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5454      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the argument list of {@code filter}
5455      *          does not match the return type of target as described above
5456      */
5457     public static MethodHandle filterReturnValue(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle filter) {
5458         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5459         MethodType filterType = filter.type();
5460         filterReturnValueChecks(targetType, filterType);
5461         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5462         BasicType rtype = BasicType.basicType(filterType.returnType());
5463         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().filterReturnForm(rtype, false);
5464         MethodType newType = targetType.changeReturnType(filterType.returnType());
5465         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, filter);
5466         return result;
5467     }
5468 
5469     private static void filterReturnValueChecks(MethodType targetType, MethodType filterType) throws RuntimeException {
5470         Class<?> rtype = targetType.returnType();
5471         int filterValues = filterType.parameterCount();
5472         if (filterValues == 0
5473                 ? (rtype != void.class)
5474                 : (rtype != filterType.parameterType(0) || filterValues != 1))
5475             throw newIllegalArgumentException("target and filter types do not match", targetType, filterType);
5476     }
5477 
5478     /**
5479      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing
5480      * some of its arguments, and then calling the target with
5481      * the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original
5482      * sequence of arguments.
5483      * <p>
5484      * The pre-processing is performed by {@code combiner}, a second method handle.
5485      * Of the arguments passed to the adapter, the first {@code N} arguments
5486      * are copied to the combiner, which is then called.
5487      * (Here, {@code N} is defined as the parameter count of the combiner.)
5488      * After this, control passes to the target, with any result
5489      * from the combiner inserted before the original {@code N} incoming
5490      * arguments.
5491      * <p>
5492      * If the combiner returns a value, the first parameter type of the target
5493      * must be identical with the return type of the combiner, and the next
5494      * {@code N} parameter types of the target must exactly match the parameters
5495      * of the combiner.
5496      * <p>
5497      * If the combiner has a void return, no result will be inserted,
5498      * and the first {@code N} parameter types of the target
5499      * must exactly match the parameters of the combiner.
5500      * <p>
5501      * The resulting adapter is the same type as the target, except that the
5502      * first parameter type is dropped,
5503      * if it corresponds to the result of the combiner.
5504      * <p>
5505      * (Note that {@link #dropArguments(MethodHandle,int,List) dropArguments} can be used to remove any arguments
5506      * that either the combiner or the target does not wish to receive.
5507      * If some of the incoming arguments are destined only for the combiner,
5508      * consider using {@link MethodHandle#asCollector asCollector} instead, since those
5509      * arguments will not need to be live on the stack on entry to the
5510      * target.)
5511      * <p><b>Example:</b>
5512      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5513 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5514 import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5515 ...
5516 MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5517   "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5518     .bindTo(System.out);
5519 MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5520   "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5521 assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5522 MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, trace);
5523 // also prints "boo":
5524 assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5525      * }</pre></blockquote>
5526      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5527      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5528      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5529      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5530      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5531      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5532      * position. {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types and values of the
5533      * {@code target} parameters and arguments that follow the folded parameters
5534      * and arguments.
5535      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5536      * // there are N arguments in A...
5537      * T target(V, A[N]..., B...);
5538      * V combiner(A...);
5539      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5540      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5541      *   return target(v, a..., b...);
5542      * }
5543      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5544      * T target2(A[N]..., B...);
5545      * void combiner2(A...);
5546      * T adapter2(A... a, B... b) {
5547      *   combiner2(a...);
5548      *   return target2(a..., b...);
5549      * }
5550      * }</pre></blockquote>
5551      * <p>
5552      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5553      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5554      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5555      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5556      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5557      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5558      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code combiner}'s return type
5559      *          is non-void and not the same as the first argument type of
5560      *          the target, or if the initial {@code N} argument types
5561      *          of the target
5562      *          (skipping one matching the {@code combiner}'s return type)
5563      *          are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}
5564      */
5565     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle combiner) {
5566         return foldArguments(target, 0, combiner);
5567     }
5568 
5569     /**
5570      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, starting at a given position, and then
5571      * calling the target with the result of the pre-processing, inserted into the original sequence of arguments just
5572      * before the folded arguments.
5573      * <p>
5574      * This method is closely related to {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}, but allows to control the
5575      * position in the parameter list at which folding takes place. The argument controlling this, {@code pos}, is a
5576      * zero-based index. The aforementioned method {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)} assumes position
5577      * 0.
5578      *
5579      * @apiNote Example:
5580      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5581     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodHandles.*;
5582     import static java.lang.invoke.MethodType.*;
5583     ...
5584     MethodHandle trace = publicLookup().findVirtual(java.io.PrintStream.class,
5585     "println", methodType(void.class, String.class))
5586     .bindTo(System.out);
5587     MethodHandle cat = lookup().findVirtual(String.class,
5588     "concat", methodType(String.class, String.class));
5589     assertEquals("boojum", (String) cat.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5590     MethodHandle catTrace = foldArguments(cat, 1, trace);
5591     // also prints "jum":
5592     assertEquals("boojum", (String) catTrace.invokeExact("boo", "jum"));
5593      * }</pre></blockquote>
5594      * <p>Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5595      * represents the result type of the {@code target} and resulting adapter.
5596      * {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type and value of the parameter and argument
5597      * of {@code target} that precedes the folding position; {@code V} also is
5598      * the result type of the {@code combiner}. {@code A}/{@code a} denote the
5599      * types and values of the {@code N} parameters and arguments at the folding
5600      * position. {@code Z}/{@code z} and {@code B}/{@code b} represent the types
5601      * and values of the {@code target} parameters and arguments that precede and
5602      * follow the folded parameters and arguments starting at {@code pos},
5603      * respectively.
5604      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5605      * // there are N arguments in A...
5606      * T target(Z..., V, A[N]..., B...);
5607      * V combiner(A...);
5608      * T adapter(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5609      *   V v = combiner(a...);
5610      *   return target(z..., v, a..., b...);
5611      * }
5612      * // and if the combiner has a void return:
5613      * T target2(Z..., A[N]..., B...);
5614      * void combiner2(A...);
5615      * T adapter2(Z... z, A... a, B... b) {
5616      *   combiner2(a...);
5617      *   return target2(z..., a..., b...);
5618      * }
5619      * }</pre></blockquote>
5620      * <p>
5621      * <em>Note:</em> The resulting adapter is never a {@linkplain MethodHandle#asVarargsCollector
5622      * variable-arity method handle}, even if the original target method handle was.
5623      *
5624      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5625      * @param pos the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5626      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5627      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5628      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5629      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5630      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5631      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5632      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5633      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at position {@code pos} of the target signature (skipping one matching
5634      *              the {@code combiner}'s return type) are not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5635      *
5636      * @see #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5637      * @since 9
5638      */
5639     public static MethodHandle foldArguments(MethodHandle target, int pos, MethodHandle combiner) {
5640         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5641         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5642         Class<?> rtype = foldArgumentChecks(pos, targetType, combinerType);
5643         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5644         boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5645         LambdaForm lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + pos, dropResult, combinerType.basicType());
5646         MethodType newType = targetType;
5647         if (!dropResult) {
5648             newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(pos, pos + 1);
5649         }
5650         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5651         return result;
5652     }
5653 
5654     private static Class<?> foldArgumentChecks(int foldPos, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType) {
5655         int foldArgs   = combinerType.parameterCount();
5656         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5657         int foldVals = rtype == void.class ? 0 : 1;
5658         int afterInsertPos = foldPos + foldVals;
5659         boolean ok = (targetType.parameterCount() >= afterInsertPos + foldArgs);
5660         if (ok) {
5661             for (int i = 0; i < foldArgs; i++) {
5662                 if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(i + afterInsertPos)) {
5663                     ok = false;
5664                     break;
5665                 }
5666             }
5667         }
5668         if (ok && foldVals != 0 && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(foldPos))
5669             ok = false;
5670         if (!ok)
5671             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5672         return rtype;
5673     }
5674 
5675     /**
5676      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, then calling the target with the result
5677      * of the pre-processing replacing the argument at the given position.
5678      *
5679      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5680      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5681      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5682      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5683      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5684      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5685      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5686      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5687      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is not the same as the argument type at position
5688      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5689      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature are
5690      *              not identical with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5691      */
5692     /*non-public*/
5693     static MethodHandle filterArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5694         return argumentsWithCombiner(true, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5695     }
5696 
5697     /**
5698      * Adapts a target method handle by pre-processing some of its arguments, calling the target with the result of
5699      * the pre-processing inserted into the original sequence of arguments at the given position.
5700      *
5701      * @param target the method handle to invoke after arguments are combined
5702      * @param position the position at which to start folding and at which to insert the folding result; if this is {@code
5703      *            0}, the effect is the same as for {@link #foldArguments(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)}.
5704      * @param combiner method handle to call initially on the incoming arguments
5705      * @param argPositions indexes of the target to pick arguments sent to the combiner from
5706      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified argument folding logic
5707      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5708      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if either of the following two conditions holds:
5709      *          (1) {@code combiner}'s return type is non-{@code void} and not the same as the argument type at position
5710      *              {@code pos} of the target signature;
5711      *          (2) the {@code N} argument types at positions {@code argPositions[1...N]} of the target signature
5712      *              (skipping {@code position} where the {@code combiner}'s return will be folded in) are not identical
5713      *              with the argument types of {@code combiner}.
5714      */
5715     /*non-public*/
5716     static MethodHandle foldArgumentsWithCombiner(MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5717         return argumentsWithCombiner(false, target, position, combiner, argPositions);
5718     }
5719 
5720     private static MethodHandle argumentsWithCombiner(boolean filter, MethodHandle target, int position, MethodHandle combiner, int ... argPositions) {
5721         MethodType targetType = target.type();
5722         MethodType combinerType = combiner.type();
5723         Class<?> rtype = argumentsWithCombinerChecks(position, filter, targetType, combinerType, argPositions);
5724         BoundMethodHandle result = target.rebind();
5725 
5726         MethodType newType = targetType;
5727         LambdaForm lform;
5728         if (filter) {
5729             lform = result.editor().filterArgumentsForm(1 + position, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5730         } else {
5731             boolean dropResult = rtype == void.class;
5732             lform = result.editor().foldArgumentsForm(1 + position, dropResult, combinerType.basicType(), argPositions);
5733             if (!dropResult) {
5734                 newType = newType.dropParameterTypes(position, position + 1);
5735             }
5736         }
5737         result = result.copyWithExtendL(newType, lform, combiner);
5738         return result;
5739     }
5740 
5741     private static Class<?> argumentsWithCombinerChecks(int position, boolean filter, MethodType targetType, MethodType combinerType, int ... argPos) {
5742         int combinerArgs = combinerType.parameterCount();
5743         if (argPos.length != combinerArgs) {
5744             throw newIllegalArgumentException("combiner and argument map must be equal size", combinerType, argPos.length);
5745         }
5746         Class<?> rtype = combinerType.returnType();
5747 
5748         for (int i = 0; i < combinerArgs; i++) {
5749             int arg = argPos[i];
5750             if (arg < 0 || arg > targetType.parameterCount()) {
5751                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("arg outside of target parameterRange", targetType, arg);
5752             }
5753             if (combinerType.parameterType(i) != targetType.parameterType(arg)) {
5754                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("target argument type at position " + arg
5755                         + " must match combiner argument type at index " + i + ": " + targetType
5756                         + " -> " + combinerType + ", map: " + Arrays.toString(argPos));
5757             }
5758         }
5759         if (filter && combinerType.returnType() != targetType.parameterType(position)) {
5760             throw misMatchedTypes("target and combiner types", targetType, combinerType);
5761         }
5762         return rtype;
5763     }
5764 
5765     /**
5766      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5767      * by guarding it with a test, a boolean-valued method handle.
5768      * If the guard fails, a fallback handle is called instead.
5769      * All three method handles must have the same corresponding
5770      * argument and return types, except that the return type
5771      * of the test must be boolean, and the test is allowed
5772      * to have fewer arguments than the other two method handles.
5773      * <p>
5774      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5775      * represents the uniform result type of the three involved handles;
5776      * {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of the {@code target}
5777      * parameters and arguments that are consumed by the {@code test}; and
5778      * {@code B}/{@code b}, those types and values of the {@code target}
5779      * parameters and arguments that are not consumed by the {@code test}.
5780      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5781      * boolean test(A...);
5782      * T target(A...,B...);
5783      * T fallback(A...,B...);
5784      * T adapter(A... a,B... b) {
5785      *   if (test(a...))
5786      *     return target(a..., b...);
5787      *   else
5788      *     return fallback(a..., b...);
5789      * }
5790      * }</pre></blockquote>
5791      * Note that the test arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5792      * be modified by execution of the test, and so are passed unchanged
5793      * from the caller to the target or fallback as appropriate.
5794      * @param test method handle used for test, must return boolean
5795      * @param target method handle to call if test passes
5796      * @param fallback method handle to call if test fails
5797      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified if/then/else logic
5798      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5799      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code test} does not return boolean,
5800      *          or if all three method types do not match (with the return
5801      *          type of {@code test} changed to match that of the target).
5802      */
5803     public static MethodHandle guardWithTest(MethodHandle test,
5804                                MethodHandle target,
5805                                MethodHandle fallback) {
5806         MethodType gtype = test.type();
5807         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5808         MethodType ftype = fallback.type();
5809         if (!ttype.equals(ftype))
5810             throw misMatchedTypes("target and fallback types", ttype, ftype);
5811         if (gtype.returnType() != boolean.class)
5812             throw newIllegalArgumentException("guard type is not a predicate "+gtype);
5813         List<Class<?>> targs = ttype.parameterList();
5814         test = dropArgumentsToMatch(test, 0, targs, 0, true);
5815         if (test == null) {
5816             throw misMatchedTypes("target and test types", ttype, gtype);
5817         }
5818         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithTest(test, target, fallback);
5819     }
5820 
5821     static <T> RuntimeException misMatchedTypes(String what, T t1, T t2) {
5822         return newIllegalArgumentException(what + " must match: " + t1 + " != " + t2);
5823     }
5824 
5825     /**
5826      * Makes a method handle which adapts a target method handle,
5827      * by running it inside an exception handler.
5828      * If the target returns normally, the adapter returns that value.
5829      * If an exception matching the specified type is thrown, the fallback
5830      * handle is called instead on the exception, plus the original arguments.
5831      * <p>
5832      * The target and handler must have the same corresponding
5833      * argument and return types, except that handler may omit trailing arguments
5834      * (similarly to the predicate in {@link #guardWithTest guardWithTest}).
5835      * Also, the handler must have an extra leading parameter of {@code exType} or a supertype.
5836      * <p>
5837      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting adapter. In the code, {@code T}
5838      * represents the return type of the {@code target} and {@code handler},
5839      * and correspondingly that of the resulting adapter; {@code A}/{@code a},
5840      * the types and values of arguments to the resulting handle consumed by
5841      * {@code handler}; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the
5842      * resulting handle discarded by {@code handler}.
5843      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
5844      * T target(A..., B...);
5845      * T handler(ExType, A...);
5846      * T adapter(A... a, B... b) {
5847      *   try {
5848      *     return target(a..., b...);
5849      *   } catch (ExType ex) {
5850      *     return handler(ex, a...);
5851      *   }
5852      * }
5853      * }</pre></blockquote>
5854      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
5855      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
5856      * from the caller to the handler, if the handler is invoked.
5857      * <p>
5858      * The target and handler must return the same type, even if the handler
5859      * always throws.  (This might happen, for instance, because the handler
5860      * is simulating a {@code finally} clause).
5861      * To create such a throwing handler, compose the handler creation logic
5862      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
5863      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
5864      * @param target method handle to call
5865      * @param exType the type of exception which the handler will catch
5866      * @param handler method handle to call if a matching exception is thrown
5867      * @return method handle which incorporates the specified try/catch logic
5868      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
5869      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code handler} does not accept
5870      *          the given exception type, or if the method handle types do
5871      *          not match in their return types and their
5872      *          corresponding parameters
5873      * @see MethodHandles#tryFinally(MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
5874      */
5875     public static MethodHandle catchException(MethodHandle target,
5876                                 Class<? extends Throwable> exType,
5877                                 MethodHandle handler) {
5878         MethodType ttype = target.type();
5879         MethodType htype = handler.type();
5880         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5881             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5882         if (htype.parameterCount() < 1 ||
5883             !htype.parameterType(0).isAssignableFrom(exType))
5884             throw newIllegalArgumentException("handler does not accept exception type "+exType);
5885         if (htype.returnType() != ttype.returnType())
5886             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler return types", ttype, htype);
5887         handler = dropArgumentsToMatch(handler, 1, ttype.parameterList(), 0, true);
5888         if (handler == null) {
5889             throw misMatchedTypes("target and handler types", ttype, htype);
5890         }
5891         return MethodHandleImpl.makeGuardWithCatch(target, exType, handler);
5892     }
5893 
5894     /**
5895      * Produces a method handle which will throw exceptions of the given {@code exType}.
5896      * The method handle will accept a single argument of {@code exType},
5897      * and immediately throw it as an exception.
5898      * The method type will nominally specify a return of {@code returnType}.
5899      * The return type may be anything convenient:  It doesn't matter to the
5900      * method handle's behavior, since it will never return normally.
5901      * @param returnType the return type of the desired method handle
5902      * @param exType the parameter type of the desired method handle
5903      * @return method handle which can throw the given exceptions
5904      * @throws NullPointerException if either argument is null
5905      */
5906     public static MethodHandle throwException(Class<?> returnType, Class<? extends Throwable> exType) {
5907         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(exType))
5908             throw new ClassCastException(exType.getName());
5909         return MethodHandleImpl.throwException(methodType(returnType, exType));
5910     }
5911 
5912     /**
5913      * Constructs a method handle representing a loop with several loop variables that are updated and checked upon each
5914      * iteration. Upon termination of the loop due to one of the predicates, a corresponding finalizer is run and
5915      * delivers the loop's result, which is the return value of the resulting handle.
5916      * <p>
5917      * Intuitively, every loop is formed by one or more "clauses", each specifying a local <em>iteration variable</em> and/or a loop
5918      * exit. Each iteration of the loop executes each clause in order. A clause can optionally update its iteration
5919      * variable; it can also optionally perform a test and conditional loop exit. In order to express this logic in
5920      * terms of method handles, each clause will specify up to four independent actions:<ul>
5921      * <li><em>init:</em> Before the loop executes, the initialization of an iteration variable {@code v} of type {@code V}.
5922      * <li><em>step:</em> When a clause executes, an update step for the iteration variable {@code v}.
5923      * <li><em>pred:</em> When a clause executes, a predicate execution to test for loop exit.
5924      * <li><em>fini:</em> If a clause causes a loop exit, a finalizer execution to compute the loop's return value.
5925      * </ul>
5926      * The full sequence of all iteration variable types, in clause order, will be notated as {@code (V...)}.
5927      * The values themselves will be {@code (v...)}.  When we speak of "parameter lists", we will usually
5928      * be referring to types, but in some contexts (describing execution) the lists will be of actual values.
5929      * <p>
5930      * Some of these clause parts may be omitted according to certain rules, and useful default behavior is provided in
5931      * this case. See below for a detailed description.
5932      * <p>
5933      * <em>Parameters optional everywhere:</em>
5934      * Each clause function is allowed but not required to accept a parameter for each iteration variable {@code v}.
5935      * As an exception, the init functions cannot take any {@code v} parameters,
5936      * because those values are not yet computed when the init functions are executed.
5937      * Any clause function may neglect to take any trailing subsequence of parameters it is entitled to take.
5938      * In fact, any clause function may take no arguments at all.
5939      * <p>
5940      * <em>Loop parameters:</em>
5941      * A clause function may take all the iteration variable values it is entitled to, in which case
5942      * it may also take more trailing parameters. Such extra values are called <em>loop parameters</em>,
5943      * with their types and values notated as {@code (A...)} and {@code (a...)}.
5944      * These become the parameters of the resulting loop handle, to be supplied whenever the loop is executed.
5945      * (Since init functions do not accept iteration variables {@code v}, any parameter to an
5946      * init function is automatically a loop parameter {@code a}.)
5947      * As with iteration variables, clause functions are allowed but not required to accept loop parameters.
5948      * These loop parameters act as loop-invariant values visible across the whole loop.
5949      * <p>
5950      * <em>Parameters visible everywhere:</em>
5951      * Each non-init clause function is permitted to observe the entire loop state, because it can be passed the full
5952      * list {@code (v... a...)} of current iteration variable values and incoming loop parameters.
5953      * The init functions can observe initial pre-loop state, in the form {@code (a...)}.
5954      * Most clause functions will not need all of this information, but they will be formally connected to it
5955      * as if by {@link #dropArguments}.
5956      * <a id="astar"></a>
5957      * More specifically, we shall use the notation {@code (V*)} to express an arbitrary prefix of a full
5958      * sequence {@code (V...)} (and likewise for {@code (v*)}, {@code (A*)}, {@code (a*)}).
5959      * In that notation, the general form of an init function parameter list
5960      * is {@code (A*)}, and the general form of a non-init function parameter list is {@code (V*)} or {@code (V... A*)}.
5961      * <p>
5962      * <em>Checking clause structure:</em>
5963      * Given a set of clauses, there is a number of checks and adjustments performed to connect all the parts of the
5964      * loop. They are spelled out in detail in the steps below. In these steps, every occurrence of the word "must"
5965      * corresponds to a place where {@link IllegalArgumentException} will be thrown if the required constraint is not
5966      * met by the inputs to the loop combinator.
5967      * <p>
5968      * <em>Effectively identical sequences:</em>
5969      * <a id="effid"></a>
5970      * A parameter list {@code A} is defined to be <em>effectively identical</em> to another parameter list {@code B}
5971      * if {@code A} and {@code B} are identical, or if {@code A} is shorter and is identical with a proper prefix of {@code B}.
5972      * When speaking of an unordered set of parameter lists, we say they the set is "effectively identical"
5973      * as a whole if the set contains a longest list, and all members of the set are effectively identical to
5974      * that longest list.
5975      * For example, any set of type sequences of the form {@code (V*)} is effectively identical,
5976      * and the same is true if more sequences of the form {@code (V... A*)} are added.
5977      * <p>
5978      * <em>Step 0: Determine clause structure.</em><ol type="a">
5979      * <li>The clause array (of type {@code MethodHandle[][]}) must be non-{@code null} and contain at least one element.
5980      * <li>The clause array may not contain {@code null}s or sub-arrays longer than four elements.
5981      * <li>Clauses shorter than four elements are treated as if they were padded by {@code null} elements to length
5982      * four. Padding takes place by appending elements to the array.
5983      * <li>Clauses with all {@code null}s are disregarded.
5984      * <li>Each clause is treated as a four-tuple of functions, called "init", "step", "pred", and "fini".
5985      * </ol>
5986      * <p>
5987      * <em>Step 1A: Determine iteration variable types {@code (V...)}.</em><ol type="a">
5988      * <li>The iteration variable type for each clause is determined using the clause's init and step return types.
5989      * <li>If both functions are omitted, there is no iteration variable for the corresponding clause ({@code void} is
5990      * used as the type to indicate that). If one of them is omitted, the other's return type defines the clause's
5991      * iteration variable type. If both are given, the common return type (they must be identical) defines the clause's
5992      * iteration variable type.
5993      * <li>Form the list of return types (in clause order), omitting all occurrences of {@code void}.
5994      * <li>This list of types is called the "iteration variable types" ({@code (V...)}).
5995      * </ol>
5996      * <p>
5997      * <em>Step 1B: Determine loop parameters {@code (A...)}.</em><ul>
5998      * <li>Examine and collect init function parameter lists (which are of the form {@code (A*)}).
5999      * <li>Examine and collect the suffixes of the step, pred, and fini parameter lists, after removing the iteration variable types.
6000      * (They must have the form {@code (V... A*)}; collect the {@code (A*)} parts only.)
6001      * <li>Do not collect suffixes from step, pred, and fini parameter lists that do not begin with all the iteration variable types.
6002      * (These types will be checked in step 2, along with all the clause function types.)
6003      * <li>Omitted clause functions are ignored.  (Equivalently, they are deemed to have empty parameter lists.)
6004      * <li>All of the collected parameter lists must be effectively identical.
6005      * <li>The longest parameter list (which is necessarily unique) is called the "external parameter list" ({@code (A...)}).
6006      * <li>If there is no such parameter list, the external parameter list is taken to be the empty sequence.
6007      * <li>The combined list consisting of iteration variable types followed by the external parameter types is called
6008      * the "internal parameter list".
6009      * </ul>
6010      * <p>
6011      * <em>Step 1C: Determine loop return type.</em><ol type="a">
6012      * <li>Examine fini function return types, disregarding omitted fini functions.
6013      * <li>If there are no fini functions, the loop return type is {@code void}.
6014      * <li>Otherwise, the common return type {@code R} of the fini functions (their return types must be identical) defines the loop return
6015      * type.
6016      * </ol>
6017      * <p>
6018      * <em>Step 1D: Check other types.</em><ol type="a">
6019      * <li>There must be at least one non-omitted pred function.
6020      * <li>Every non-omitted pred function must have a {@code boolean} return type.
6021      * </ol>
6022      * <p>
6023      * <em>Step 2: Determine parameter lists.</em><ol type="a">
6024      * <li>The parameter list for the resulting loop handle will be the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6025      * <li>The parameter list for init functions will be adjusted to the external parameter list.
6026      * (Note that their parameter lists are already effectively identical to this list.)
6027      * <li>The parameter list for every non-omitted, non-init (step, pred, and fini) function must be
6028      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list {@code (V... A...)}.
6029      * </ol>
6030      * <p>
6031      * <em>Step 3: Fill in omitted functions.</em><ol type="a">
6032      * <li>If an init function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the clause's iteration variable
6033      * type.
6034      * <li>If a step function is omitted, use an {@linkplain #identity identity function} of the clause's iteration
6035      * variable type; insert dropped argument parameters before the identity function parameter for the non-{@code void}
6036      * iteration variables of preceding clauses. (This will turn the loop variable into a local loop invariant.)
6037      * <li>If a pred function is omitted, use a constant {@code true} function. (This will keep the loop going, as far
6038      * as this clause is concerned.  Note that in such cases the corresponding fini function is unreachable.)
6039      * <li>If a fini function is omitted, use a {@linkplain #empty default value} for the
6040      * loop return type.
6041      * </ol>
6042      * <p>
6043      * <em>Step 4: Fill in missing parameter types.</em><ol type="a">
6044      * <li>At this point, every init function parameter list is effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)},
6045      * but some lists may be shorter. For every init function with a short parameter list, pad out the end of the list.
6046      * <li>At this point, every non-init function parameter list is effectively identical to the internal parameter
6047      * list {@code (V... A...)}, but some lists may be shorter. For every non-init function with a short parameter list,
6048      * pad out the end of the list.
6049      * <li>Argument lists are padded out by {@linkplain #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int) dropping unused trailing arguments}.
6050      * </ol>
6051      * <p>
6052      * <em>Final observations.</em><ol type="a">
6053      * <li>After these steps, all clauses have been adjusted by supplying omitted functions and arguments.
6054      * <li>All init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (A...)}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6055      * <li>All fini functions have a common return type {@code R}, which the final loop handle will also have.
6056      * <li>All non-init functions have a common parameter type list {@code (V... A...)}, of
6057      * (non-{@code void}) iteration variables {@code V} followed by loop parameters.
6058      * <li>Each pair of init and step functions agrees in their return type {@code V}.
6059      * <li>Each non-init function will be able to observe the current values {@code (v...)} of all iteration variables.
6060      * <li>Every function will be able to observe the incoming values {@code (a...)} of all loop parameters.
6061      * </ol>
6062      * <p>
6063      * <em>Example.</em> As a consequence of step 1A above, the {@code loop} combinator has the following property:
6064      * <ul>
6065      * <li>Given {@code N} clauses {@code Cn = {null, Sn, Pn}} with {@code n = 1..N}.
6066      * <li>Suppose predicate handles {@code Pn} are either {@code null} or have no parameters.
6067      * (Only one {@code Pn} has to be non-{@code null}.)
6068      * <li>Suppose step handles {@code Sn} have signatures {@code (B1..BX)Rn}, for some constant {@code X>=N}.
6069      * <li>Suppose {@code Q} is the count of non-void types {@code Rn}, and {@code (V1...VQ)} is the sequence of those types.
6070      * <li>It must be that {@code Vn == Bn} for {@code n = 1..min(X,Q)}.
6071      * <li>The parameter types {@code Vn} will be interpreted as loop-local state elements {@code (V...)}.
