6072      * <li>Any remaining types {@code BQ+1..BX} (if {@code Q<X}) will determine
6073      * the resulting loop handle's parameter types {@code (A...)}.
6074      * </ul>
6075      * In this example, the loop handle parameters {@code (A...)} were derived from the step functions,
6076      * which is natural if most of the loop computation happens in the steps.  For some loops,
6077      * the burden of computation might be heaviest in the pred functions, and so the pred functions
6078      * might need to accept the loop parameter values.  For loops with complex exit logic, the fini
6079      * functions might need to accept loop parameters, and likewise for loops with complex entry logic,
6080      * where the init functions will need the extra parameters.  For such reasons, the rules for
6081      * determining these parameters are as symmetric as possible, across all clause parts.
6082      * In general, the loop parameters function as common invariant values across the whole
6083      * loop, while the iteration variables function as common variant values, or (if there is
6084      * no step function) as internal loop invariant temporaries.
6085      * <p>
6086      * <em>Loop execution.</em><ol type="a">
6087      * <li>When the loop is called, the loop input values are saved in locals, to be passed to
6088      * every clause function. These locals are loop invariant.
6089      * <li>Each init function is executed in clause order (passing the external arguments {@code (a...)})
6090      * and the non-{@code void} values are saved (as the iteration variables {@code (v...)}) into locals.
6091      * These locals will be loop varying (unless their steps behave as identity functions, as noted above).
6092      * <li>All function executions (except init functions) will be passed the internal parameter list, consisting of
6093      * the non-{@code void} iteration values {@code (v...)} (in clause order) and then the loop inputs {@code (a...)}
6094      * (in argument order).
6095      * <li>The step and pred functions are then executed, in clause order (step before pred), until a pred function
6096      * returns {@code false}.
6097      * <li>The non-{@code void} result from a step function call is used to update the corresponding value in the
6098      * sequence {@code (v...)} of loop variables.
6099      * The updated value is immediately visible to all subsequent function calls.
6100      * <li>If a pred function returns {@code false}, the corresponding fini function is called, and the resulting value
6101      * (of type {@code R}) is returned from the loop as a whole.
6102      * <li>If all the pred functions always return true, no fini function is ever invoked, and the loop cannot exit
6103      * except by throwing an exception.
6104      * </ol>
6105      * <p>
6106      * <em>Usage tips.</em>
6107      * <ul>
6108      * <li>Although each step function will receive the current values of <em>all</em> the loop variables,
6109      * sometimes a step function only needs to observe the current value of its own variable.
6110      * In that case, the step function may need to explicitly {@linkplain #dropArguments drop all preceding loop variables}.
6111      * This will require mentioning their types, in an expression like {@code dropArguments(step, 0, V0.class, ...)}.
6112      * <li>Loop variables are not required to vary; they can be loop invariant.  A clause can create
6113      * a loop invariant by a suitable init function with no step, pred, or fini function.  This may be
6114      * useful to "wire" an incoming loop argument into the step or pred function of an adjacent loop variable.
6115      * <li>If some of the clause functions are virtual methods on an instance, the instance
6116      * itself can be conveniently placed in an initial invariant loop "variable", using an initial clause
6117      * like {@code new MethodHandle[]{identity(ObjType.class)}}.  In that case, the instance reference
6118      * will be the first iteration variable value, and it will be easy to use virtual
6119      * methods as clause parts, since all of them will take a leading instance reference matching that value.
6120      * </ul>
6121      * <p>
6122      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. As above, {@code V} and {@code v} represent the types
6123      * and values of loop variables; {@code A} and {@code a} represent arguments passed to the whole loop;
6124      * and {@code R} is the common result type of all finalizers as well as of the resulting loop.
6125      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6126      * V... init...(A...);
6127      * boolean pred...(V..., A...);
6128      * V... step...(V..., A...);
6129      * R fini...(V..., A...);
6130      * R loop(A... a) {
6131      *   V... v... = init...(a...);
6132      *   for (;;) {
6133      *     for ((v, p, s, f) in (v..., pred..., step..., fini...)) {
6134      *       v = s(v..., a...);
6135      *       if (!p(v..., a...)) {
6136      *         return f(v..., a...);
6137      *       }
6138      *     }
6139      *   }
6140      * }
6141      * }</pre></blockquote>
6142      * Note that the parameter type lists {@code (V...)} and {@code (A...)} have been expanded
6143      * to their full length, even though individual clause functions may neglect to take them all.
6144      * As noted above, missing parameters are filled in as if by {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}.
6145      *
6146      * @apiNote Example:
6147      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6148      * // iterative implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6149      * static int one(int k) { return 1; }
6150      * static int inc(int i, int acc, int k) { return i + 1; }
6151      * static int mult(int i, int acc, int k) { return i * acc; }
6152      * static boolean pred(int i, int acc, int k) { return i < k; }
6153      * static int fin(int i, int acc, int k) { return acc; }
6154      * // assume MH_one, MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6155      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6156      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6157      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6158      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6159      * assertEquals(120, loop.invoke(5));
6160      * }</pre></blockquote>
6161      * The same example, dropping arguments and using combinators:
6162      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6163      * // simplified implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6164      * static int inc(int i) { return i + 1; } // drop acc, k
6165      * static int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; } //drop k
6166      * static boolean cmp(int i, int k) { return i < k; }
6167      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, and MH_cmp are handles to the above methods
6168      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6169      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6170      * MethodHandle MH_pred = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MH_cmp, 1, int.class); // drop acc
6171      * MethodHandle MH_fin = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 0, int.class); // drop i
6172      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6173      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6174      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6175      * assertEquals(720, loop.invoke(6));
6176      * }</pre></blockquote>
6177      * A similar example, using a helper object to hold a loop parameter:
6178      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6179      * // instance-based implementation of the factorial function as a loop handle
6180      * static class FacLoop {
6181      *   final int k;
6182      *   FacLoop(int k) { this.k = k; }
6183      *   int inc(int i) { return i + 1; }
6184      *   int mult(int i, int acc) { return i * acc; }
6185      *   boolean pred(int i) { return i < k; }
6186      *   int fin(int i, int acc) { return acc; }
6187      * }
6188      * // assume MH_FacLoop is a handle to the constructor
6189      * // assume MH_inc, MH_mult, MH_pred, and MH_fin are handles to the above methods
6190      * // null initializer for counter, should initialize to 0
6191      * MethodHandle MH_one = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 1);
6192      * MethodHandle[] instanceClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_FacLoop};
6193      * MethodHandle[] counterClause = new MethodHandle[]{null, MH_inc};
6194      * MethodHandle[] accumulatorClause = new MethodHandle[]{MH_one, MH_mult, MH_pred, MH_fin};
6195      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.loop(instanceClause, counterClause, accumulatorClause);
6196      * assertEquals(5040, loop.invoke(7));
6197      * }</pre></blockquote>
6198      *
6199      * @param clauses an array of arrays (4-tuples) of {@link MethodHandle}s adhering to the rules described above.
6200      *
6201      * @return a method handle embodying the looping behavior as defined by the arguments.
6202      *
6203      * @throws IllegalArgumentException in case any of the constraints described above is violated.
6204      *
6205      * @see MethodHandles#whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6206      * @see MethodHandles#doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6207      * @see MethodHandles#countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6208      * @see MethodHandles#iteratedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6209      * @since 9
6210      */
6211     public static MethodHandle loop(MethodHandle[]... clauses) {
6212         // Step 0: determine clause structure.
6213         loopChecks0(clauses);
6214 
6215         List<MethodHandle> init = new ArrayList<>();
6216         List<MethodHandle> step = new ArrayList<>();
6217         List<MethodHandle> pred = new ArrayList<>();
6218         List<MethodHandle> fini = new ArrayList<>();
6219 
6220         Stream.of(clauses).filter(c -> Stream.of(c).anyMatch(Objects::nonNull)).forEach(clause -> {
6221             init.add(clause[0]); // all clauses have at least length 1
6222             step.add(clause.length <= 1 ? null : clause[1]);
6223             pred.add(clause.length <= 2 ? null : clause[2]);
6224             fini.add(clause.length <= 3 ? null : clause[3]);
6225         });
6226 
6227         assert Stream.of(init, step, pred, fini).map(List::size).distinct().count() == 1;
6228         final int nclauses = init.size();
6229 
6230         // Step 1A: determine iteration variables (V...).
6231         final List<Class<?>> iterationVariableTypes = new ArrayList<>();
6232         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6233             MethodHandle in = init.get(i);
6234             MethodHandle st = step.get(i);
6235             if (in == null && st == null) {
6236                 iterationVariableTypes.add(void.class);
6237             } else if (in != null && st != null) {
6238                 loopChecks1a(i, in, st);
6239                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in.type().returnType());
6240             } else {
6241                 iterationVariableTypes.add(in == null ? st.type().returnType() : in.type().returnType());
6242             }
6243         }
6244         final List<Class<?>> commonPrefix = iterationVariableTypes.stream().filter(t -> t != void.class).
6245                 collect(Collectors.toList());
6246 
6247         // Step 1B: determine loop parameters (A...).
6248         final List<Class<?>> commonSuffix = buildCommonSuffix(init, step, pred, fini, commonPrefix.size());
6249         loopChecks1b(init, commonSuffix);
6250 
6251         // Step 1C: determine loop return type.
6252         // Step 1D: check other types.
6253         // local variable required here; see JDK-8223553
6254         Stream<Class<?>> cstream = fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type)
6255                 .map(MethodType::returnType);
6256         final Class<?> loopReturnType = cstream.findFirst().orElse(void.class);
6257         loopChecks1cd(pred, fini, loopReturnType);
6258 
6259         // Step 2: determine parameter lists.
6260         final List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence = new ArrayList<>(commonPrefix);
6261         commonParameterSequence.addAll(commonSuffix);
6262         loopChecks2(step, pred, fini, commonParameterSequence);
6263 
6264         // Step 3: fill in omitted functions.
6265         for (int i = 0; i < nclauses; ++i) {
6266             Class<?> t = iterationVariableTypes.get(i);
6267             if (init.get(i) == null) {
6268                 init.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonSuffix)));
6269             }
6270             if (step.get(i) == null) {
6271                 step.set(i, dropArgumentsToMatch(identityOrVoid(t), 0, commonParameterSequence, i));
6272             }
6273             if (pred.get(i) == null) {
6274                 pred.set(i, dropArguments0(constant(boolean.class, true), 0, commonParameterSequence));
6275             }
6276             if (fini.get(i) == null) {
6277                 fini.set(i, empty(methodType(t, commonParameterSequence)));
6278             }
6279         }
6280 
6281         // Step 4: fill in missing parameter types.
6282         // Also convert all handles to fixed-arity handles.
6283         List<MethodHandle> finit = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(init, commonSuffix));
6284         List<MethodHandle> fstep = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(step, commonParameterSequence));
6285         List<MethodHandle> fpred = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(pred, commonParameterSequence));
6286         List<MethodHandle> ffini = fixArities(fillParameterTypes(fini, commonParameterSequence));
6287 
6288         assert finit.stream().map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6289                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonSuffix));
6290         assert Stream.of(fstep, fpred, ffini).flatMap(List::stream).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::parameterList).
6291                 allMatch(pl -> pl.equals(commonParameterSequence));
6292 
6293         return MethodHandleImpl.makeLoop(loopReturnType, commonSuffix, finit, fstep, fpred, ffini);
6294     }
6295 
6296     private static void loopChecks0(MethodHandle[][] clauses) {
6297         if (clauses == null || clauses.length == 0) {
6298             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null or no clauses passed");
6299         }
6300         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(Objects::isNull)) {
6301             throw newIllegalArgumentException("null clauses are not allowed");
6302         }
6303         if (Stream.of(clauses).anyMatch(c -> c.length > 4)) {
6304             throw newIllegalArgumentException("All loop clauses must be represented as MethodHandle arrays with at most 4 elements.");
6305         }
6306     }
6307 
6308     private static void loopChecks1a(int i, MethodHandle in, MethodHandle st) {
6309         if (in.type().returnType() != st.type().returnType()) {
6310             throw misMatchedTypes("clause " + i + ": init and step return types", in.type().returnType(),
6311                     st.type().returnType());
6312         }
6313     }
6314 
6315     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(Stream<MethodHandle> mhs, int skipSize) {
6316         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6317         final List<Class<?>> longest = mhs.filter(Objects::nonNull).
6318                 // take only those that can contribute to a common suffix because they are longer than the prefix
6319                         map(MethodHandle::type).
6320                         filter(t -> t.parameterCount() > skipSize).
6321                         map(MethodType::parameterList).
6322                         reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6323         return longest.size() == 0 ? empty : longest.subList(skipSize, longest.size());
6324     }
6325 
6326     private static List<Class<?>> longestParameterList(List<List<Class<?>>> lists) {
6327         final List<Class<?>> empty = List.of();
6328         return lists.stream().reduce((p, q) -> p.size() >= q.size() ? p : q).orElse(empty);
6329     }
6330 
6331     private static List<Class<?>> buildCommonSuffix(List<MethodHandle> init, List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, int cpSize) {
6332         final List<Class<?>> longest1 = longestParameterList(Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream), cpSize);
6333         final List<Class<?>> longest2 = longestParameterList(init.stream(), 0);
6334         return longestParameterList(Arrays.asList(longest1, longest2));
6335     }
6336 
6337     private static void loopChecks1b(List<MethodHandle> init, List<Class<?>> commonSuffix) {
6338         if (init.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6339                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonSuffix))) {
6340             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical init parameter type lists: " + init +
6341                     " (common suffix: " + commonSuffix + ")");
6342         }
6343     }
6344 
6345     private static void loopChecks1cd(List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, Class<?> loopReturnType) {
6346         if (fini.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6347                 anyMatch(t -> t != loopReturnType)) {
6348             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-identical finalizer return types: " + fini + " (return type: " +
6349                     loopReturnType + ")");
6350         }
6351 
6352         if (!pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).findFirst().isPresent()) {
6353             throw newIllegalArgumentException("no predicate found", pred);
6354         }
6355         if (pred.stream().filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).map(MethodType::returnType).
6356                 anyMatch(t -> t != boolean.class)) {
6357             throw newIllegalArgumentException("predicates must have boolean return type", pred);
6358         }
6359     }
6360 
6361     private static void loopChecks2(List<MethodHandle> step, List<MethodHandle> pred, List<MethodHandle> fini, List<Class<?>> commonParameterSequence) {
6362         if (Stream.of(step, pred, fini).flatMap(List::stream).filter(Objects::nonNull).map(MethodHandle::type).
6363                 anyMatch(t -> !t.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, commonParameterSequence))) {
6364             throw newIllegalArgumentException("found non-effectively identical parameter type lists:\nstep: " + step +
6365                     "\npred: " + pred + "\nfini: " + fini + " (common parameter sequence: " + commonParameterSequence + ")");
6366         }
6367     }
6368 
6369     private static List<MethodHandle> fillParameterTypes(List<MethodHandle> hs, final List<Class<?>> targetParams) {
6370         return hs.stream().map(h -> {
6371             int pc = h.type().parameterCount();
6372             int tpsize = targetParams.size();
6373             return pc < tpsize ? dropArguments0(h, pc, targetParams.subList(pc, tpsize)) : h;
6374         }).collect(Collectors.toList());
6375     }
6376 
6377     private static List<MethodHandle> fixArities(List<MethodHandle> hs) {
6378         return hs.stream().map(MethodHandle::asFixedArity).collect(Collectors.toList());
6379     }
6380 
6381     /**
6382      * Constructs a {@code while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6383      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6384      * <p>
6385      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6386      * method will, in each iteration, first evaluate the predicate and then execute its body (if the predicate
6387      * evaluates to {@code true}).
6388      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} (the body will not be executed in this case).
6389      * <p>
6390      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6391      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6392      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6393      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6394      * <p>
6395      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6396      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6397      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6398      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6399      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6400      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6401      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6402      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6403      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6404      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6405      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6406      * additional state variable of the loop.
6407      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6408      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6409      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6410      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6411      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6412      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6413      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6414      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6415      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6416      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6417      * </ul>
6418      * <p>
6419      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6420      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6421      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6422      * from the external parameter list.
6423      * </ul>
6424      * <p>
6425      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6426      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6427      * passed to the loop.
6428      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6429      * V init(A...);
6430      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6431      * V body(V, A...);
6432      * V whileLoop(A... a...) {
6433      *   V v = init(a...);
6434      *   while (pred(v, a...)) {
6435      *     v = body(v, a...);
6436      *   }
6437      *   return v;
6438      * }
6439      * }</pre></blockquote>
6440      *
6441      * @apiNote Example:
6442      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6443      * // implement the zip function for lists as a loop handle
6444      * static List<String> initZip(Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return new ArrayList<>(); }
6445      * static boolean zipPred(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) { return a.hasNext() && b.hasNext(); }
6446      * static List<String> zipStep(List<String> zip, Iterator<String> a, Iterator<String> b) {
6447      *   zip.add(a.next());
6448      *   zip.add(b.next());
6449      *   return zip;
6450      * }
6451      * // assume MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, and MH_zipStep are handles to the above methods
6452      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.whileLoop(MH_initZip, MH_zipPred, MH_zipStep);
6453      * List<String> a = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d");
6454      * List<String> b = Arrays.asList("e", "f", "g", "h");
6455      * List<String> zipped = Arrays.asList("a", "e", "b", "f", "c", "g", "d", "h");
6456      * assertEquals(zipped, (List<String>) loop.invoke(a.iterator(), b.iterator()));
6457      * }</pre></blockquote>
6458      *
6459      *
6460      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6461      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6462      * MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6463      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6464      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6465      *     MethodHandle[]
6466      *         checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini },
6467      *         varBody   = { init, body };
6468      *     return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6469      * }
6470      * }</pre></blockquote>
6471      *
6472      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6473      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6474      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6475      *             above for other constraints.
6476      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6477      *             See above for other constraints.
6478      *
6479      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6480      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6481      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6482      *
6483      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6484      * @see #doWhileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6485      * @since 9
6486      */
6487     public static MethodHandle whileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6488         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6489         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6490         MethodHandle[] checkExit = { null, null, pred, fini };
6491         MethodHandle[] varBody = { init, body };
6492         return loop(checkExit, varBody);
6493     }
6494 
6495     /**
6496      * Constructs a {@code do-while} loop from an initializer, a body, and a predicate.
6497      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6498      * <p>
6499      * The {@code pred} handle describes the loop condition; and {@code body}, its body. The loop resulting from this
6500      * method will, in each iteration, first execute its body and then evaluate the predicate.
6501      * The loop will terminate once the predicate evaluates to {@code false} after an execution of the body.
6502      * <p>
6503      * The {@code init} handle describes the initial value of an additional optional loop-local variable.
6504      * In each iteration, this loop-local variable, if present, will be passed to the {@code body}
6505      * and updated with the value returned from its invocation. The result of loop execution will be
6506      * the final value of the additional loop-local variable (if present).
6507      * <p>
6508      * The following rules hold for these argument handles:<ul>
6509      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6510      * {@code (V A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (A...)void}.
6511      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6512      * and we will write {@code (V A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6513      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (A...)V}.)
6514      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V A...)} of the body is called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6515      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6516      * <li>If the iteration variable type {@code V} is dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6517      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6518      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6519      * additional state variable of the loop.
6520      * The body must both accept and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6521      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6522      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6523      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6524      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6525      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6526      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6527      * <li>The {@code pred} handle must not be {@code null}.  It must have {@code boolean} as its return type.
6528      * Its parameter list (either empty or of the form {@code (V A*)}) must be
6529      * effectively identical to the internal parameter list.
6530      * </ul>
6531      * <p>
6532      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6533      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6534      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6535      * from the external parameter list.
6536      * </ul>
6537      * <p>
6538      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6539      * the sole loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A}/{@code a}, that of the argument
6540      * passed to the loop.
6541      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6542      * V init(A...);
6543      * boolean pred(V, A...);
6544      * V body(V, A...);
6545      * V doWhileLoop(A... a...) {
6546      *   V v = init(a...);
6547      *   do {
6548      *     v = body(v, a...);
6549      *   } while (pred(v, a...));
6550      *   return v;
6551      * }
6552      * }</pre></blockquote>
6553      *
6554      * @apiNote Example:
6555      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6556      * // int i = 0; while (i < limit) { ++i; } return i; => limit
6557      * static int zero(int limit) { return 0; }
6558      * static int step(int i, int limit) { return i + 1; }
6559      * static boolean pred(int i, int limit) { return i < limit; }
6560      * // assume MH_zero, MH_step, and MH_pred are handles to the above methods
6561      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.doWhileLoop(MH_zero, MH_step, MH_pred);
6562      * assertEquals(23, loop.invoke(23));
6563      * }</pre></blockquote>
6564      *
6565      *
6566      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6567      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6568      * MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6569      *     MethodHandle fini = (body.type().returnType() == void.class
6570      *                         ? null : identity(body.type().returnType()));
6571      *     MethodHandle[] clause = { init, body, pred, fini };
6572      *     return loop(clause);
6573      * }
6574      * }</pre></blockquote>
6575      *
6576      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6577      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6578      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}. It controls the loop parameters and result type.
6579      *             See above for other constraints.
6580      * @param pred condition for the loop, which may not be {@code null}. Its result type must be {@code boolean}. See
6581      *             above for other constraints.
6582      *
6583      * @return a method handle implementing the {@code while} loop as described by the arguments.
6584      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if the rules for the arguments are violated.
6585      * @throws NullPointerException if {@code pred} or {@code body} are {@code null}.
6586      *
6587      * @see #loop(MethodHandle[][])
6588      * @see #whileLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6589      * @since 9
6590      */
6591     public static MethodHandle doWhileLoop(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body, MethodHandle pred) {
6592         whileLoopChecks(init, pred, body);
6593         MethodHandle fini = identityOrVoid(body.type().returnType());
6594         MethodHandle[] clause = {init, body, pred, fini };
6595         return loop(clause);
6596     }
6597 
6598     private static void whileLoopChecks(MethodHandle init, MethodHandle pred, MethodHandle body) {
6599         Objects.requireNonNull(pred);
6600         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6601         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6602         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6603         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6604         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList;
6605         if (returnType == void.class) {
6606             // OK
6607         } else if (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType) {
6608             // leading V argument missing => error
6609             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6610             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6611         } else {
6612             outerList = innerList.subList(1, innerList.size());
6613         }
6614         MethodType predType = pred.type();
6615         if (predType.returnType() != boolean.class ||
6616                 !predType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, innerList)) {
6617             throw misMatchedTypes("loop predicate", predType, methodType(boolean.class, innerList));
6618         }
6619         if (init != null) {
6620             MethodType initType = init.type();
6621             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6622                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6623                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6624             }
6625         }
6626     }
6627 
6628     /**
6629      * Constructs a loop that runs a given number of iterations.
6630      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6631      * <p>
6632      * The number of iterations is determined by the {@code iterations} handle evaluation result.
6633      * The loop counter {@code i} is an extra loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6634      * It will be initialized to 0 and incremented by 1 in each iteration.
6635      * <p>
6636      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6637      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6638      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6639      * <p>
6640      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6641      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6642      * iteration variable.
6643      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6644      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6645      * <p>
6646      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6647      * <li>The {@code iterations} handle must not be {@code null}, and must return
6648      * the type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6649      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6650      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6651      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6652      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6653      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6654      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6655      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6656      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6657      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6658      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6659      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterations} handle.
6660      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6661      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6662      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6663      * additional state variable of the loop.
6664      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6665      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6666      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6667      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6668      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6669      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6670      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6671      * <li>The parameter list of {@code iterations} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6672      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6673      * </ul>
6674      * <p>
6675      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6676      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6677      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6678      * from the external parameter list.
6679      * </ul>
6680      * <p>
6681      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6682      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6683      * arguments passed to the loop.
6684      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6685      * int iterations(A...);
6686      * V init(A...);
6687      * V body(V, int, A...);
6688      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6689      *   int end = iterations(a...);
6690      *   V v = init(a...);
6691      *   for (int i = 0; i < end; ++i) {
6692      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6693      *   }
6694      *   return v;
6695      * }
6696      * }</pre></blockquote>
6697      *
6698      * @apiNote Example with a fully conformant body method:
6699      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6700      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6701      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6702      * static String step(String v, int counter, String init) { return "na " + v; }
6703      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6704      * MethodHandle fit13 = MethodHandles.constant(int.class, 13);
6705      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.identity(String.class);
6706      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(fit13, start, MH_step);
6707      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("Lambdaman!"));
6708      * }</pre></blockquote>
6709      *
6710      * @apiNote Example with the simplest possible body method type,
6711      * and passing the number of iterations to the loop invocation:
6712      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6713      * // String s = "Lambdaman!"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = "na " + s; } return s;
6714      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6715      * static String step(String v, int counter ) { return "na " + v; }
6716      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6717      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(int.class), 1, String.class);
6718      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class);
6719      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i) -> "na " + v
6720      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "Lambdaman!"));
6721      * }</pre></blockquote>
6722      *
6723      * @apiNote Example that treats the number of iterations, string to append to, and string to append
6724      * as loop parameters:
6725      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6726      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6727      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6728      * static String step(String v, int counter, int iterations_, String pre, String start_) { return pre + " " + v; }
6729      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6730      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.identity(int.class);
6731      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArguments(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, int.class, String.class);
6732      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, MH_step);  // (v, i, _, pre, _) -> pre + " " + v
6733      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke(13, "na", "Lambdaman!"));
6734      * }</pre></blockquote>
6735      *
6736      * @apiNote Example that illustrates the usage of {@link #dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandle, int, List, int)}
6737      * to enforce a loop type:
6738      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6739      * // String s = "Lambdaman!", t = "na"; for (int i = 0; i < 13; ++i) { s = t + " " + s; } return s;
6740      * // => a variation on a well known theme
6741      * static String step(String v, int counter, String pre) { return pre + " " + v; }
6742      * // assume MH_step is a handle to the method above
6743      * MethodType loopType = methodType(String.class, String.class, int.class, String.class);
6744      * MethodHandle count = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(int.class),    0, loopType.parameterList(), 1);
6745      * MethodHandle start = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MethodHandles.identity(String.class), 0, loopType.parameterList(), 2);
6746      * MethodHandle body  = MethodHandles.dropArgumentsToMatch(MH_step,                              2, loopType.parameterList(), 0);
6747      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.countedLoop(count, start, body);  // (v, i, pre, _, _) -> pre + " " + v
6748      * assertEquals("na na na na na na na na na na na na na Lambdaman!", loop.invoke("na", 13, "Lambdaman!"));
6749      * }</pre></blockquote>
6750      *
6751      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6752      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6753      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6754      *     return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6755      * }
6756      * }</pre></blockquote>
6757      *
6758      * @param iterations a non-{@code null} handle to return the number of iterations this loop should run. The handle's
6759      *                   result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6760      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6761      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6762      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6763      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6764      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6765      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6766      *             See above for other constraints.
6767      *
6768      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6769      * @throws NullPointerException if either of the {@code iterations} or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6770      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6771      *
6772      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6773      * @since 9
6774      */
6775     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle iterations, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6776         return countedLoop(empty(iterations.type()), iterations, init, body);
6777     }
6778 
6779     /**
6780      * Constructs a loop that counts over a range of numbers.
6781      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6782      * <p>
6783      * The loop counter {@code i} is a loop iteration variable of type {@code int}.
6784      * The {@code start} and {@code end} handles determine the start (inclusive) and end (exclusive)
6785      * values of the loop counter.
6786      * The loop counter will be initialized to the {@code int} value returned from the evaluation of the
6787      * {@code start} handle and run to the value returned from {@code end} (exclusively) with a step width of 1.
6788      * <p>
6789      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6790      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6791      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6792      * <p>
6793      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6794      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6795      * iteration variable.
6796      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6797      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6798      * <p>
6799      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6800      * <li>The {@code start} and {@code end} handles must not be {@code null}, and must both return
6801      * the common type {@code int}, referred to here as {@code I} in parameter type lists.
6802      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6803      * {@code (V I A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (I A...)void}.
6804      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6805      * and we will write {@code (V I A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6806      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (I A...)V}.)
6807      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V I A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6808      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6809      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6810      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code I} types,
6811      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6812      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code end} handle.
6813      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V I)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
6814      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
6815      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
6816      * additional state variable of the loop.
6817      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
6818      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
6819      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
6820      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
6821      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6822      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
6823      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
6824      * <li>The parameter list of {@code start} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
6825      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
6826      * <li>Likewise, the parameter list of {@code end} must be effectively identical
6827      * to the external parameter list.
6828      * </ul>
6829      * <p>
6830      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
6831      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
6832      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
6833      * from the external parameter list.
6834      * </ul>
6835      * <p>
6836      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
6837      * the second loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent
6838      * arguments passed to the loop.
6839      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6840      * int start(A...);
6841      * int end(A...);
6842      * V init(A...);
6843      * V body(V, int, A...);
6844      * V countedLoop(A... a...) {
6845      *   int e = end(a...);
6846      *   int s = start(a...);
6847      *   V v = init(a...);
6848      *   for (int i = s; i < e; ++i) {
6849      *     v = body(v, i, a...);
6850      *   }
6851      *   return v;
6852      * }
6853      * }</pre></blockquote>
6854      *
6855      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed as follows:
6856      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
6857      * MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6858      *     MethodHandle returnVar = dropArguments(identity(init.type().returnType()), 0, int.class, int.class);
6859      *     // assume MH_increment and MH_predicate are handles to implementation-internal methods with
6860      *     // the following semantics:
6861      *     // MH_increment: (int limit, int counter) -> counter + 1
6862      *     // MH_predicate: (int limit, int counter) -> counter < limit
6863      *     Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int
6864      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
6865      *     MethodHandle incr = MH_increment, pred = MH_predicate, retv = null;
6866      *     if (returnType != void.class) {  // ignore the V variable
6867      *         incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6868      *         pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6869      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType); // ignore limit
6870      *     }
6871      *     body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6872      *     MethodHandle[]
6873      *         loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6874      *         bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6875      *         indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6876      *     return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6877      * }
6878      * }</pre></blockquote>
6879      *
6880      * @param start a non-{@code null} handle to return the start value of the loop counter, which must be {@code int}.
6881      *              See above for other constraints.
6882      * @param end a non-{@code null} handle to return the end value of the loop counter (the loop will run to
6883      *            {@code end-1}). The result type must be {@code int}. See above for other constraints.
6884      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
6885      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
6886      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
6887      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
6888      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus an {@code int} parameter (for the counter),
6889      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
6890      *             See above for other constraints.
6891      *
6892      * @return a method handle representing the loop.
6893      * @throws NullPointerException if any of the {@code start}, {@code end}, or {@code body} handles is {@code null}.
6894      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the rules formulated above.
6895      *
6896      * @see #countedLoop(MethodHandle, MethodHandle, MethodHandle)
6897      * @since 9
6898      */
6899     public static MethodHandle countedLoop(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6900         countedLoopChecks(start, end, init, body);
6901         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();  // int, but who's counting?
6902         Class<?> limitType   = end.type().returnType();    // yes, int again
6903         Class<?> returnType  = body.type().returnType();
6904         MethodHandle incr = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopStep);
6905         MethodHandle pred = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_countedLoopPred);
6906         MethodHandle retv = null;
6907         if (returnType != void.class) {
6908             incr = dropArguments(incr, 1, returnType);  // (limit, v, i) => (limit, i)
6909             pred = dropArguments(pred, 1, returnType);  // ditto
6910             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, counterType);
6911         }
6912         body = dropArguments(body, 0, counterType);  // ignore the limit variable
6913         MethodHandle[]
6914             loopLimit  = { end, null, pred, retv }, // limit = end(); i < limit || return v
6915             bodyClause = { init, body },            // v = init(); v = body(v, i)
6916             indexVar   = { start, incr };           // i = start(); i = i + 1
6917         return loop(loopLimit, bodyClause, indexVar);
6918     }
6919 
6920     private static void countedLoopChecks(MethodHandle start, MethodHandle end, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
6921         Objects.requireNonNull(start);
6922         Objects.requireNonNull(end);
6923         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
6924         Class<?> counterType = start.type().returnType();
6925         if (counterType != int.class) {
6926             MethodType expected = start.type().changeReturnType(int.class);
6927             throw misMatchedTypes("start function", start.type(), expected);
6928         } else if (end.type().returnType() != counterType) {
6929             MethodType expected = end.type().changeReturnType(counterType);
6930             throw misMatchedTypes("end function", end.type(), expected);
6931         }
6932         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
6933         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
6934         List<Class<?>> innerList = bodyType.parameterList();
6935         // strip leading V value if present
6936         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
6937         if (vsize != 0 && (innerList.size() == 0 || innerList.get(0) != returnType)) {
6938             // argument list has no "V" => error
6939             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
6940             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6941         } else if (innerList.size() <= vsize || innerList.get(vsize) != counterType) {
6942             // missing I type => error
6943             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, counterType);
6944             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
6945         }
6946         List<Class<?>> outerList = innerList.subList(vsize + 1, innerList.size());
6947         if (outerList.isEmpty()) {
6948             // special case; take lists from end handle
6949             outerList = end.type().parameterList();
6950             innerList = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize + 1, outerList).parameterList();
6951         }
6952         MethodType expected = methodType(counterType, outerList);
6953         if (!start.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6954             throw misMatchedTypes("start parameter types", start.type(), expected);
6955         }
6956         if (end.type() != start.type() &&
6957             !end.type().effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6958             throw misMatchedTypes("end parameter types", end.type(), expected);
6959         }
6960         if (init != null) {
6961             MethodType initType = init.type();
6962             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
6963                 !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, outerList)) {
6964                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, outerList));
6965             }
6966         }
6967     }
6968 
6969     /**
6970      * Constructs a loop that ranges over the values produced by an {@code Iterator<T>}.
6971      * This is a convenience wrapper for the {@linkplain #loop(MethodHandle[][]) generic loop combinator}.
6972      * <p>
6973      * The iterator itself will be determined by the evaluation of the {@code iterator} handle.
6974      * Each value it produces will be stored in a loop iteration variable of type {@code T}.
6975      * <p>
6976      * If the {@code body} handle returns a non-{@code void} type {@code V}, a leading loop iteration variable
6977      * of that type is also present.  This variable is initialized using the optional {@code init} handle,
6978      * or to the {@linkplain #empty default value} of type {@code V} if that handle is {@code null}.
6979      * <p>
6980      * In each iteration, the iteration variables are passed to an invocation of the {@code body} handle.
6981      * A non-{@code void} value returned from the body (of type {@code V}) updates the leading
6982      * iteration variable.
6983      * The result of the loop handle execution will be the final {@code V} value of that variable
6984      * (or {@code void} if there is no {@code V} variable).
6985      * <p>
6986      * The following rules hold for the argument handles:<ul>
6987      * <li>The {@code body} handle must not be {@code null}; its type must be of the form
6988      * {@code (V T A...)V}, where {@code V} is non-{@code void}, or else {@code (T A...)void}.
6989      * (In the {@code void} case, we assign the type {@code void} to the name {@code V},
6990      * and we will write {@code (V T A...)V} with the understanding that a {@code void} type {@code V}
6991      * is quietly dropped from the parameter list, leaving {@code (T A...)V}.)
6992      * <li>The parameter list {@code (V T A...)} of the body contributes to a list
6993      * of types called the <em>internal parameter list</em>.
6994      * It will constrain the parameter lists of the other loop parts.
6995      * <li>As a special case, if the body contributes only {@code V} and {@code T} types,
6996      * with no additional {@code A} types, then the internal parameter list is extended by
6997      * the argument types {@code A...} of the {@code iterator} handle; if it is {@code null} the
6998      * single type {@code Iterable} is added and constitutes the {@code A...} list.
6999      * <li>If the iteration variable types {@code (V T)} are dropped from the internal parameter list, the resulting shorter
7000      * list {@code (A...)} is called the <em>external parameter list</em>.
7001      * <li>The body return type {@code V}, if non-{@code void}, determines the type of an
7002      * additional state variable of the loop.
7003      * The body must both accept a leading parameter and return a value of this type {@code V}.
7004      * <li>If {@code init} is non-{@code null}, it must have return type {@code V}.
7005      * Its parameter list (of some <a href="MethodHandles.html#astar">form {@code (A*)}</a>) must be
7006      * <a href="MethodHandles.html#effid">effectively identical</a>
7007      * to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7008      * <li>If {@code init} is {@code null}, the loop variable will be initialized to its
7009      * {@linkplain #empty default value}.
7010      * <li>If the {@code iterator} handle is non-{@code null}, it must have the return
7011      * type {@code java.util.Iterator} or a subtype thereof.
7012      * The iterator it produces when the loop is executed will be assumed
7013      * to yield values which can be converted to type {@code T}.
7014      * <li>The parameter list of an {@code iterator} that is non-{@code null} (of some form {@code (A*)}) must be
7015      * effectively identical to the external parameter list {@code (A...)}.
7016      * <li>If {@code iterator} is {@code null} it defaults to a method handle which behaves
7017      * like {@link java.lang.Iterable#iterator()}.  In that case, the internal parameter list
7018      * {@code (V T A...)} must have at least one {@code A} type, and the default iterator
7019      * handle parameter is adjusted to accept the leading {@code A} type, as if by
7020      * the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7021      * The leading {@code A} type must be {@code Iterable} or a subtype thereof.
7022      * This conversion step, done at loop construction time, must not throw a {@code WrongMethodTypeException}.
7023      * </ul>
7024      * <p>
7025      * The type {@code T} may be either a primitive or reference.
7026      * Since type {@code Iterator<T>} is erased in the method handle representation to the raw type {@code Iterator},
7027      * the {@code iteratedLoop} combinator adjusts the leading argument type for {@code body} to {@code Object}
7028      * as if by the {@link MethodHandle#asType asType} conversion method.
7029      * Therefore, if an iterator of the wrong type appears as the loop is executed, runtime exceptions may occur
7030      * as the result of dynamic conversions performed by {@link MethodHandle#asType(MethodType)}.
7031      * <p>
7032      * The resulting loop handle's result type and parameter signature are determined as follows:<ul>
7033      * <li>The loop handle's result type is the result type {@code V} of the body.
7034      * <li>The loop handle's parameter types are the types {@code (A...)},
7035      * from the external parameter list.
7036      * </ul>
7037      * <p>
7038      * Here is pseudocode for the resulting loop handle. In the code, {@code V}/{@code v} represent the type / value of
7039      * the loop variable as well as the result type of the loop; {@code T}/{@code t}, that of the elements of the
7040      * structure the loop iterates over, and {@code A...}/{@code a...} represent arguments passed to the loop.
7041      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7042      * Iterator<T> iterator(A...);  // defaults to Iterable::iterator
7043      * V init(A...);
7044      * V body(V,T,A...);
7045      * V iteratedLoop(A... a...) {
7046      *   Iterator<T> it = iterator(a...);
7047      *   V v = init(a...);
7048      *   while (it.hasNext()) {
7049      *     T t = it.next();
7050      *     v = body(v, t, a...);
7051      *   }
7052      *   return v;
7053      * }
7054      * }</pre></blockquote>
7055      *
7056      * @apiNote Example:
7057      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7058      * // get an iterator from a list
7059      * static List<String> reverseStep(List<String> r, String e) {
7060      *   r.add(0, e);
7061      *   return r;
7062      * }
7063      * static List<String> newArrayList() { return new ArrayList<>(); }
7064      * // assume MH_reverseStep and MH_newArrayList are handles to the above methods
7065      * MethodHandle loop = MethodHandles.iteratedLoop(null, MH_newArrayList, MH_reverseStep);
7066      * List<String> list = Arrays.asList("a", "b", "c", "d", "e");
7067      * List<String> reversedList = Arrays.asList("e", "d", "c", "b", "a");
7068      * assertEquals(reversedList, (List<String>) loop.invoke(list));
7069      * }</pre></blockquote>
7070      *
7071      * @apiNote The implementation of this method can be expressed approximately as follows:
7072      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7073      * MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7074      *     // assume MH_next, MH_hasNext, MH_startIter are handles to methods of Iterator/Iterable
7075      *     Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7076      *     Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7077      *     MethodHandle nextVal = MH_next.asType(MH_next.type().changeReturnType(ttype));
7078      *     MethodHandle retv = null, step = body, startIter = iterator;
7079      *     if (returnType != void.class) {
7080      *         // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7081      *         retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7082      *         // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7083      *         step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7084      *     }
7085      *     if (startIter == null)  startIter = MH_getIter;
7086      *     MethodHandle[]
7087      *         iterVar    = { startIter, null, MH_hasNext, retv }, // it = iterator; while (it.hasNext())
7088      *         bodyClause = { init, filterArguments(step, 0, nextVal) };  // v = body(v, t, a)
7089      *     return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7090      * }
7091      * }</pre></blockquote>
7092      *
7093      * @param iterator an optional handle to return the iterator to start the loop.
7094      *                 If non-{@code null}, the handle must return {@link java.util.Iterator} or a subtype.
7095      *                 See above for other constraints.
7096      * @param init optional initializer, providing the initial value of the loop variable.
7097      *             May be {@code null}, implying a default initial value.  See above for other constraints.
7098      * @param body body of the loop, which may not be {@code null}.
7099      *             It controls the loop parameters and result type in the standard case (see above for details).
7100      *             It must accept its own return type (if non-void) plus a {@code T} parameter (for the iterated values),
7101      *             and may accept any number of additional types.
7102      *             See above for other constraints.
7103      *
7104      * @return a method handle embodying the iteration loop functionality.
7105      * @throws NullPointerException if the {@code body} handle is {@code null}.
7106      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if any argument violates the above requirements.
7107      *
7108      * @since 9
7109      */
7110     public static MethodHandle iteratedLoop(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7111         Class<?> iterableType = iteratedLoopChecks(iterator, init, body);
7112         Class<?> returnType = body.type().returnType();
7113         MethodHandle hasNext = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iteratePred);
7114         MethodHandle nextRaw = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_iterateNext);
7115         MethodHandle startIter;
7116         MethodHandle nextVal;
7117         {
7118             MethodType iteratorType;
7119             if (iterator == null) {
7120                 // derive argument type from body, if available, else use Iterable
7121                 startIter = MethodHandleImpl.getConstantHandle(MethodHandleImpl.MH_initIterator);
7122                 iteratorType = startIter.type().changeParameterType(0, iterableType);
7123             } else {
7124                 // force return type to the internal iterator class
7125                 iteratorType = iterator.type().changeReturnType(Iterator.class);
7126                 startIter = iterator;
7127             }
7128             Class<?> ttype = body.type().parameterType(returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7129             MethodType nextValType = nextRaw.type().changeReturnType(ttype);
7130 
7131             // perform the asType transforms under an exception transformer, as per spec.:
7132             try {
7133                 startIter = startIter.asType(iteratorType);
7134                 nextVal = nextRaw.asType(nextValType);
7135             } catch (WrongMethodTypeException ex) {
7136                 throw new IllegalArgumentException(ex);
7137             }
7138         }
7139 
7140         MethodHandle retv = null, step = body;
7141         if (returnType != void.class) {
7142             // the simple thing first:  in (I V A...), drop the I to get V
7143             retv = dropArguments(identity(returnType), 0, Iterator.class);
7144             // body type signature (V T A...), internal loop types (I V A...)
7145             step = swapArguments(body, 0, 1);  // swap V <-> T
7146         }
7147 
7148         MethodHandle[]
7149             iterVar    = { startIter, null, hasNext, retv },
7150             bodyClause = { init, filterArgument(step, 0, nextVal) };
7151         return loop(iterVar, bodyClause);
7152     }
7153 
7154     private static Class<?> iteratedLoopChecks(MethodHandle iterator, MethodHandle init, MethodHandle body) {
7155         Objects.requireNonNull(body);
7156         MethodType bodyType = body.type();
7157         Class<?> returnType = bodyType.returnType();
7158         List<Class<?>> internalParamList = bodyType.parameterList();
7159         // strip leading V value if present
7160         int vsize = (returnType == void.class ? 0 : 1);
7161         if (vsize != 0 && (internalParamList.size() == 0 || internalParamList.get(0) != returnType)) {
7162             // argument list has no "V" => error
7163             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(0, returnType);
7164             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7165         } else if (internalParamList.size() <= vsize) {
7166             // missing T type => error
7167             MethodType expected = bodyType.insertParameterTypes(vsize, Object.class);
7168             throw misMatchedTypes("body function", bodyType, expected);
7169         }
7170         List<Class<?>> externalParamList = internalParamList.subList(vsize + 1, internalParamList.size());
7171         Class<?> iterableType = null;
7172         if (iterator != null) {
7173             // special case; if the body handle only declares V and T then
7174             // the external parameter list is obtained from iterator handle
7175             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7176                 externalParamList = iterator.type().parameterList();
7177             }
7178             MethodType itype = iterator.type();
7179             if (!Iterator.class.isAssignableFrom(itype.returnType())) {
7180                 throw newIllegalArgumentException("iteratedLoop first argument must have Iterator return type");
7181             }
7182             if (!itype.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7183                 MethodType expected = methodType(itype.returnType(), externalParamList);
7184                 throw misMatchedTypes("iterator parameters", itype, expected);
7185             }
7186         } else {
7187             if (externalParamList.isEmpty()) {
7188                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the body handle
7189                 // only declares V and T then the external parameter list consists
7190                 // of Iterable
7191                 externalParamList = Arrays.asList(Iterable.class);
7192                 iterableType = Iterable.class;
7193             } else {
7194                 // special case; if the iterator handle is null and the external
7195                 // parameter list is not empty then the first parameter must be
7196                 // assignable to Iterable
7197                 iterableType = externalParamList.get(0);
7198                 if (!Iterable.class.isAssignableFrom(iterableType)) {
7199                     throw newIllegalArgumentException(
7200                             "inferred first loop argument must inherit from Iterable: " + iterableType);
7201                 }
7202             }
7203         }
7204         if (init != null) {
7205             MethodType initType = init.type();
7206             if (initType.returnType() != returnType ||
7207                     !initType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(0, externalParamList)) {
7208                 throw misMatchedTypes("loop initializer", initType, methodType(returnType, externalParamList));
7209             }
7210         }
7211         return iterableType;  // help the caller a bit
7212     }
7213 
7214     /*non-public*/
7215     static MethodHandle swapArguments(MethodHandle mh, int i, int j) {
7216         // there should be a better way to uncross my wires
7217         int arity = mh.type().parameterCount();
7218         int[] order = new int[arity];
7219         for (int k = 0; k < arity; k++)  order[k] = k;
7220         order[i] = j; order[j] = i;
7221         Class<?>[] types = mh.type().parameterArray();
7222         Class<?> ti = types[i]; types[i] = types[j]; types[j] = ti;
7223         MethodType swapType = methodType(mh.type().returnType(), types);
7224         return permuteArguments(mh, swapType, order);
7225     }
7226 
7227     /**
7228      * Makes a method handle that adapts a {@code target} method handle by wrapping it in a {@code try-finally} block.
7229      * Another method handle, {@code cleanup}, represents the functionality of the {@code finally} block. Any exception
7230      * thrown during the execution of the {@code target} handle will be passed to the {@code cleanup} handle. The
7231      * exception will be rethrown, unless {@code cleanup} handle throws an exception first.  The
7232      * value returned from the {@code cleanup} handle's execution will be the result of the execution of the
7233      * {@code try-finally} handle.
7234      * <p>
7235      * The {@code cleanup} handle will be passed one or two additional leading arguments.
7236      * The first is the exception thrown during the
7237      * execution of the {@code target} handle, or {@code null} if no exception was thrown.
7238      * The second is the result of the execution of the {@code target} handle, or, if it throws an exception,
7239      * a {@code null}, zero, or {@code false} value of the required type is supplied as a placeholder.
7240      * The second argument is not present if the {@code target} handle has a {@code void} return type.
7241      * (Note that, except for argument type conversions, combinators represent {@code void} values in parameter lists
7242      * by omitting the corresponding paradoxical arguments, not by inserting {@code null} or zero values.)
7243      * <p>
7244      * The {@code target} and {@code cleanup} handles must have the same corresponding argument and return types, except
7245      * that the {@code cleanup} handle may omit trailing arguments. Also, the {@code cleanup} handle must have one or
7246      * two extra leading parameters:<ul>
7247      * <li>a {@code Throwable}, which will carry the exception thrown by the {@code target} handle (if any); and
7248      * <li>a parameter of the same type as the return type of both {@code target} and {@code cleanup}, which will carry
7249      * the result from the execution of the {@code target} handle.
7250      * This parameter is not present if the {@code target} returns {@code void}.
7251      * </ul>
7252      * <p>
7253      * The pseudocode for the resulting adapter looks as follows. In the code, {@code V} represents the result type of
7254      * the {@code try/finally} construct; {@code A}/{@code a}, the types and values of arguments to the resulting
7255      * handle consumed by the cleanup; and {@code B}/{@code b}, those of arguments to the resulting handle discarded by
7256      * the cleanup.
7257      * <blockquote><pre>{@code
7258      * V target(A..., B...);
7259      * V cleanup(Throwable, V, A...);
7260      * V adapter(A... a, B... b) {
7261      *   V result = (zero value for V);
7262      *   Throwable throwable = null;
7263      *   try {
7264      *     result = target(a..., b...);
7265      *   } catch (Throwable t) {
7266      *     throwable = t;
7267      *     throw t;
7268      *   } finally {
7269      *     result = cleanup(throwable, result, a...);
7270      *   }
7271      *   return result;
7272      * }
7273      * }</pre></blockquote>
7274      * <p>
7275      * Note that the saved arguments ({@code a...} in the pseudocode) cannot
7276      * be modified by execution of the target, and so are passed unchanged
7277      * from the caller to the cleanup, if it is invoked.
7278      * <p>
7279      * The target and cleanup must return the same type, even if the cleanup
7280      * always throws.
7281      * To create such a throwing cleanup, compose the cleanup logic
7282      * with {@link #throwException throwException},
7283      * in order to create a method handle of the correct return type.
7284      * <p>
7285      * Note that {@code tryFinally} never converts exceptions into normal returns.
7286      * In rare cases where exceptions must be converted in that way, first wrap
7287      * the target with {@link #catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)}
7288      * to capture an outgoing exception, and then wrap with {@code tryFinally}.
7289      * <p>
7290      * It is recommended that the first parameter type of {@code cleanup} be
7291      * declared {@code Throwable} rather than a narrower subtype.  This ensures
7292      * {@code cleanup} will always be invoked with whatever exception that
7293      * {@code target} throws.  Declaring a narrower type may result in a
7294      * {@code ClassCastException} being thrown by the {@code try-finally}
7295      * handle if the type of the exception thrown by {@code target} is not
7296      * assignable to the first parameter type of {@code cleanup}.  Note that
7297      * various exception types of {@code VirtualMachineError},
7298      * {@code LinkageError}, and {@code RuntimeException} can in principle be
7299      * thrown by almost any kind of Java code, and a finally clause that
7300      * catches (say) only {@code IOException} would mask any of the others
7301      * behind a {@code ClassCastException}.
7302      *
7303      * @param target the handle whose execution is to be wrapped in a {@code try} block.
7304      * @param cleanup the handle that is invoked in the finally block.
7305      *
7306      * @return a method handle embodying the {@code try-finally} block composed of the two arguments.
7307      * @throws NullPointerException if any argument is null
7308      * @throws IllegalArgumentException if {@code cleanup} does not accept
7309      *          the required leading arguments, or if the method handle types do
7310      *          not match in their return types and their
7311      *          corresponding trailing parameters
7312      *
7313      * @see MethodHandles#catchException(MethodHandle, Class, MethodHandle)
7314      * @since 9
7315      */
7316     public static MethodHandle tryFinally(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7317         List<Class<?>> targetParamTypes = target.type().parameterList();
7318         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7319 
7320         tryFinallyChecks(target, cleanup);
7321 
7322         // Match parameter lists: if the cleanup has a shorter parameter list than the target, add ignored arguments.
7323         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7324         // target parameter list.
7325         cleanup = dropArgumentsToMatch(cleanup, (rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2), targetParamTypes, 0);
7326 
7327         // Ensure that the intrinsic type checks the instance thrown by the
7328         // target against the first parameter of cleanup
7329         cleanup = cleanup.asType(cleanup.type().changeParameterType(0, Throwable.class));
7330 
7331         // Use asFixedArity() to avoid unnecessary boxing of last argument for VarargsCollector case.
7332         return MethodHandleImpl.makeTryFinally(target.asFixedArity(), cleanup.asFixedArity(), rtype, targetParamTypes);
7333     }
7334 
7335     private static void tryFinallyChecks(MethodHandle target, MethodHandle cleanup) {
7336         Class<?> rtype = target.type().returnType();
7337         if (rtype != cleanup.type().returnType()) {
7338             throw misMatchedTypes("target and return types", cleanup.type().returnType(), rtype);
7339         }
7340         MethodType cleanupType = cleanup.type();
7341         if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(cleanupType.parameterType(0))) {
7342             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup first argument and Throwable", cleanup.type(), Throwable.class);
7343         }
7344         if (rtype != void.class && cleanupType.parameterType(1) != rtype) {
7345             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup second argument and target return type", cleanup.type(), rtype);
7346         }
7347         // The cleanup parameter list (minus the leading Throwable and result parameters) must be a sublist of the
7348         // target parameter list.
7349         int cleanupArgIndex = rtype == void.class ? 1 : 2;
7350         if (!cleanupType.effectivelyIdenticalParameters(cleanupArgIndex, target.type().parameterList())) {
7351             throw misMatchedTypes("cleanup parameters after (Throwable,result) and target parameter list prefix",
7352                     cleanup.type(), target.type());
7353         }
7354     }
